O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the derivative of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I have finished it by its explanations and through its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is foreign to everyone, thus the science is lost and hidden, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have made.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed, and the science is obscured.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it along with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will come together with the forms of the instruments of cauterization, and of the other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and of preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes to master the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and the forms and the conjunctions and separations of them, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and brains and the number of them, and the movement and rest of the veins, both moving and resting, and from where they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this Hippocrates said that the name is not much, and the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and we place in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, should be careful that he does not fall into error and that he does not harm men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	so I have seen many of those who practice this science and if they abandon their knowledge and their experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut the abscess of scruples or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone of a man with a fistula, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he removed with it a piece of the bladder, and the man was dead within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen it happen that the vein was called for by the surgeon, and I saw the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if one cut well he died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another physician who took in care the duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breakage a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the physicians blamed ignorance for holding the breakage on the wound by strong binding, and did not leave the wound to form a scab, and left it thus until the end;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that it not be untied;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and remained thus until the leg became entirely swollen and the foot, and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was summoned to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had untied it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all along the corruption has already been confirmed in the member, and it cannot be cured.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption does not cease to spread through the member as long as the member is completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And you will see another miracle that will dissolve the enclosed abscess, and then will inflame it due to the wickedness of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For abscess, when it is full of melancholic humor, it does not matter that one touches it with iron if it is not in a place where one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear sons, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, attention or there is danger in many arrangements;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary that you guard yourself, so that foolish people cannot speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take your arms in caution, and undertake your ailments lightly and firmly, and make use of the better way so that by the grace of God you come to health and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let go of the diseases causing fearful and grievous suffering;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your arms from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says distinctly in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take a foolish doctor to cure an illness, lest you be called a foolish person.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about cauterization by fire and also about cauterization by sharp medicine, and it is the chapter organized from the head to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the forms of the instruments, and of the iron tools for cauterization, and of all that which is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and of ulcers and wounds, and of extractions of arrowheads, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapters are ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring the dislocations and the twistings, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the lowest part of the feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we begin our work, it is fitting that we describe the quality of aid and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and of harm, are a long and subtle discourse and secret response;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and from this speaking the many wise men agree with it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and do not suffice for them my words, for I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to know the hot and moist complexion, and the dry and moist complexion.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion with assembled matter, they disagreed about nothing and said that cautery is of great aid;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not suitable for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot illness with heat, nor with dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and it is far from what they say who claim the opposite, that cautery provides great aid to hot and dry illnesses that occur in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of man and its moisture according to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true many times by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in no way does it interfere with those who have tried it, and who know by long practice the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the experience of the tension;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the members gather and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that gathering fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cauterization with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and does not come except to the member that is burned, and does not harm another member unless by bad name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines come from one member to another by touching, and bring to the sick member diseases of grievous sanitation;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire by its height and by the goodness of its substance does not do evil, if there is not excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself for the length of the speech, for it does not please me that I reveal to you the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree on what time the cauterizations should be done, and choose taking pains.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the sudden and hidden injuries are better cured with the help of cauterization;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and meanwhile the cauterizations are for necessary pains and haste that cannot wait for the time when a greater evil may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think, dear son, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is healed by cauterization has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it to him thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they believe, because cauterizations are not a medicine that changes the temperament, and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for the haste of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and of its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes from the patient's temperament and the location of the disease and its strength;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered in him the excesses by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless fire cauterization is administered to him or he has a little of excess and moisture, such as cauterization of teeth for the pain, and similar things, and that pain does not come back;
mais ce avient poc.	but that happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures for a disease and they are not effective, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	It appears well that cauterizations are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauterizations with instruments of gold are better than those of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of the gold and because of the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the places of cauterization do not become infected, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauterizations of gold are worth more than those of iron, as they praised them.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And however when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know how hot it is by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	it becomes disfigured by the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we will use the fire cautery that we have made appear in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have organized this chapter from head to foot, because the path should be easier to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are good for moisture and for cold on the brain, and in it is done because of the cause of an illness called "soda", and by the cause of many humors which descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and due to a multitude of noises and pain of teeth and pain of throat, and similarly for all illnesses that come from cold such as paralysis and soddeness and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine, cleansing the head three or four times, according to what the strength and the age and the habituation of the patient can endure;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient relax their head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make them sit crossed between your hands, and put their hands on their chest;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterwards place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and then take your two thumbs, if it bleeds from inside then heat the cautery that is called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put it on the left side of the incision, and make descending and constricting movements with your hand little by little in a twisting manner;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your right hand gently, and look at the place if you see the bone a little bit;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, restart the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a little wax, and put it in warm and soft cotton inside, and put it on the wound, and let it be for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After a dead person, put a moist cloth on the belly;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it stay there until the chill is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing the wound of the joint which is called "tetrafarmaçon", as long as it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the old ones said that the more a wound suppurates, the more it will clean itself;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason it is helped by movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should cauterize so much that part of the bone is burned, and then scrape away what is burned from the bone, and it will be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the others said that one should cauterize so much on it, and hit it so hard that one removes from the bone as large a piece as the buckle that women put on their belts, so that the humors come out freely;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must let the wound remain covered for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that, one must clean and suck it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two kinds of cauterizations do not seem to me to be good in every respect, unless in certain men in whom there is a way of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I must leave the dead skin;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by the continuous flow of nature, as we demonstrate in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and myself when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more healthy and beneficial for me, and in that case I observe a healthy outcome.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in the whole head there comes chronic pain, and it lasts a long time, then the patient must use hiera and pills which are called "cochia", and purging of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if they do the cauterization that we have said before, it is of no value.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the sick person's arm is of strong nature, and that it not be too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize the finger with the same cautery that we have spoken of above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards do the cautery on each horn of the head just to the bone, as we have said before, and do the cautery on the spot which is called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where one applies warm poultices;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lead your hand so that you do not see to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head there comes sudden pain, and the disease extends to the eye, and the head is purged with medicines that cleanse, and one has done the other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of diseases, and all this does not help.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then one makes cauteries according to two methods, that is to say with hot medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of hot medicine is that you take a handful of alum, and remove the outer layer and scrape it from the head, and then make an application on the temple where the pain is held in such a manner that you can apply the handful of alum under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is applied, bind it and constrain it well and leave it thus for 12 hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then unbind it and pull out the handful of alum, and leave the wound thus for 2 or 3 days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then put a needle on the ankle, thrusting it into the flesh until the marrow can be extracted.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of a fracture, as long as it is healing;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that I have written about certain burning medications, or the treatment of burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cauterization with iron is according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a nail or it has little curvature, and in the middle has a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and twist the iron a little gently, until the half of the spear head that is to be cauterized is dry;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and raise your hand so that the artery does not become inflamed, which is deplorable, and causes an abundance of blood to flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After put cotton in a ditch of seat, and put sewer on the place for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I put moist cotton on the wound, and then treat the place with oil until it is healthy;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migration with the cautery that is called "cultellare", to the entire point, and beware of touching the artery in this migration which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the migration
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migration as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous saying of medicine and of iron does not suffice for it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery that is called "cultellare" until it becomes white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and sign thus on the aching place a line of half a thumb in length, and put your hand once, and strain that you do not touch the artery and that you do not approach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware of the jaw that moves when one chews, and the nerves do not have regard for what moves and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the decrement of blood from the artery when it will be cut, or cutting that causes great fear and discomfort to the one who does not know it, and who is not a studied and experienced person.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work in the middle of the way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it is helpful.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have spoken of in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cauterization that has two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and is this cautery better than the others and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain from cold comes in the ear, and one has opened it with solutive medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "points", of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncturing all around the ailing ear, or around the two where the pain is held in both, and one extracts a little from beneath the root of the ear after you have signed the place of the wound;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and let there be X points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure, the place as long as it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be cured by a cautery is not other than those which move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of the diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cauterization on similarities that come from hemorrhoids and spasms of the kidneys.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this kind of torture that comes from flow of blood and purging of the head and gargling, and it does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauterizations:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cauterization on the part that brings forth blood, and make him be cauterized behind the head of the ear a little above the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cauterization on for as long as it seems to you that the heart is being loosened;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the scalpel that we previously mentioned, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the blade be a bit thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After curing the limb as I have previously said, as long as it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When a head injury is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the vessel which is called "hazels" as we have previously said, and the fourth cauterization on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be cured as we have previously said.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness it is necessary to give the patient great and pills which purify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After the patient has risen from their bed, and you have put on their occipital bone an emplaster of sinusitis that is written in the treatise of emplasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed in that place, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, then have three cauteries made on the middle of the head descending to the neck, and let there be a space of two fingers between each cautery;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and cure it like the others, and if you see that it is swollen, and the patient is suffering, then have one cautery made in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it is necessary, two others on the two corners, and cure until he is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let these cauteries be called "olivare", as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be anointed with herbs and with what we have previously mentioned;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	afterwards anoint the head of the patient, then make him a cauterization in the middle of the head and on each horn, and on the back and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you are a skilled artisan, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, then make four cauterizations on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be until the worst of the fever is gone, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until he is healthy, and let it be the cauterizations that are called "olivare" which we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not undergo cauterization except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first anoint the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient has great and suffering pain to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is an infant who cannot yet suffer, have them gargle and chew soothing the brain often with good meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king of the head in the middle, and have the cautery done according to what we said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and suffering, have them undergo cauterization as I said for the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let them be cauterized with olive oil according to the manner that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, have them undergo a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the humors are excessive or the moistures corrupted and the phlegm thick, then the cautery of such cauteries as we said for the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if it is due to the cause of melancholy that the superfluous humors are declining into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then one must give a drink of something by which the brain may be purified, according to what has been stated previously in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After reaching the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after making a plaster of linen, well done, like a circle, put it on his head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should be well crossed, and held firmly from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after applying the plaster, and it is of no use to anoint with butter of old barley;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it with tempered fire, so that the pain can be endured by the patient;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after having seen the circle within his head, and let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient every week once with good governance until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or you will see it cauterized where you make several points all around the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on cotton wet in butter and in fat of geese.
de l’awe des eulz	of the ache of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When ache first comes to the eyes by the signs that I have told in the division, then anoint and give to drink to the patient thing cleansing the head, and the warm of all moisture, and make them sweat or bathe several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After command to rub his head, and make him cauterize in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descension of the ache is to the two eyes together, or in one if the descension is in one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and let the cautery reach all the veins and arteries that are disordered beneath the heart, and be the cautery long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of decrement of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, then stain it with earth powder as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and in the incision of the cautery how you will stop them;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes they perform a cautery or a branding under the two bones of the back.
dou cors des larmes	tears of the eyes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are ancient and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head before;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic superfluities, then have the cautery done which I spoke of at the beginning of the treatise concerning the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I apply cautery to the head, and two cauteries on the temples, and two cauteries or branding irons under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is necessary to brand more, then cauterize gently above the eyebrow with one small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	two ulcers of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you administer medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit him, then give the patient three nutmegs to drink;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king of the head, and have it cauterized with half a cautery of olive oil;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries from the cautery called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, a little below the eyebrows;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the skin of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cauterization that is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	because of what this form is:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that it makes two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let your hand be still unless until the third part of the skin is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted into a membrane, and prick the eye, and one makes cauterizations in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	it is to know by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cauterization, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their birthplace, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they are born and are even, then put the patient in a healthy condition;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards sign on the skin of the eyes a figure that is as small as the funnel of the nose, and let the beginnings of the sign be among the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moist cotton in a glass of oil and anoint the eyelid with the juice of the pear, then heat the cautery of what is its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have signed little by little many times, so that the heart is set on fire in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the skin pulled back, and the hairs lifted to the tip of the eyelid;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, and let it be for three hours, then put moist cotton in a poultice as long as the numbness is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of the joint until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And after that come the hairs, and the skin is softened then reapply the cautery to the same place, just as you did previously;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are deformed, then cauterize until the skin is lifted to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The medical cauterization of burning is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as possible, then make from parchment the shape of a leaf of myrtle;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and lively chalk, of each one ounce, and mix together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it hasten, so that it does not become cold, then put it on the shape that you have made like the mold of the eye, and apply it to the skin of the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness is in one eye only, then one should treat in one, and if it is in both eyes;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put cotton wet with water on the eye;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the head of the sick person be in a warm place and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press the poultice and wet the mouth every time the sick person feels burning from the medicine, for it feels burning also like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have applied this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning sensation has passed, then lift the skin of the eye, and look to see if the skin is lifted like it was lifted by contraction of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then again put the medicine on the place where the medicine has not been applied, so that your operations are equal, and your eyes are aimed at the point;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a cotton cloth moistened in broth so that the bitter hearts are cooled, after treating the place of the joint which is called "diaphragm" and others, until it be sound.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you take good care with your work, by great care that it not happen that the point of the medicine comes to the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the oil, then reapply the medicine to that place which is softened by the proper skin, thus as you have done before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment until it is healthy;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and it is the form of the mortar of the dead:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And it is known that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this will be their conceptions;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the right way be hidden from the one to whom is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments are not profitable, then it is necessary that you do cauterization in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head on your shoulder;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does it bow its head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	afterwards put moist cotton in the hollow of the eye or juice of persicary on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After the heat of the cautery which is applied:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaved on the head in the shape of a wing of a dove, along with which is the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but in any case, that which is shaved serves for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After the fistula has been covered with a dressing, and in it put the poultice, and the dried;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and it is closed, thus the operation, and put outside the dressing;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after putting on the hot cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the nail from beneath the oil, so that your hands do not make a fool;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you apply the cautery just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then restart the cautery once more, and also if you are a master of the profession, and let it be for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After I put on a moist cotton cloth, and the treatment of the dislocation of the bone lasts as long as it is healthy, and if forty days pass and it is not healthy, then I put on a medicine, a corrosive ointment, until the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the treatment according to what will be treated in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Cut into the fistula, and make the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	afterwards put in the incision a thin rod of wax, of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make a quantity of a .Z. of poultice;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold the hand or wrist firmly, and do not move the patient's joints, so that the applied poultices do not fall from their place;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is suitable to put on the patient's oil cotton wool soaked in sheep's urine or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the poultice if it is applied near the place of the fistula, and the sound tissue through miraculous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer a probe to the navel, and to bring the fistula to the body of the navel according to what is suitable in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur cracks in the lips which are called "poil", and also in the lips of infants.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks of that which we have spoken of in divisions, and the treatment is not beneficial, then heat a small cautery iron according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And insert it hastily into these cracks until it reaches the source;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, anoint the limb with cerote until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess forms in the root of the throat or in the uvula or palate, or the roots of the teeth, after having made putridity and rottenness and it becomes swollen and develops into a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it is not beneficial:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you apply the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after closing or puncturing the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron becomes hot at the source of it, and on the rear of the limb;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in cures, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is thus cured, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then you must uncover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines and it is not effective, then put the head of the patient in a healthy position;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery whose form will come here after in such a manner that you put a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the hot cautery between the teeth hastily, and hold it so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After lifting your hand and reapplying the cauterization according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After the patient has filled his mouth with salty water, and holds it for an hour and spits it out frequently.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in the same way the tooth that was loose is confirmed, and the gum is softened and restrained, and the decaying moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or fever, and medical treatments are of no value, then it requires cauterization in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cauterization with a borings tool and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization with a borings tool is such that you hold a borings tool of iron or steel, and the tip in an iron or copper skimmer;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	After taking cotton and wrapping it around the tip of a stick, and moistening it in borings tool oil, and applying it to the aching tooth quickly and holding it until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see a wool or cotton in cold butter, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron as long as the fetid discharge comes from the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery is such that you should press an iron or copper cane, and it should be thick so that the fetid discharge does not come to the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	after heating the cautery, from which the form will come after, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be gone the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the application of this cautery, and then pull out the tooth.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and it is the form of the cauterization:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And perform cauterization on the head that you want, and according to what you have the power to do;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and it is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moistures, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterized head from which afterwards comes the form, and it has two openings for the humors to exit on the cauterization of the other part;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and put the hot cauterization on the abscess once, or as the art is, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small then put cauterization according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in this way for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on cotton moistened with butter until the abscess is opened;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure of the limbs and of tents until it be healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the canine:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors prevail over the channels of the womb, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by solvent medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after they do a cautery at the root of the throat, and beware that you not come near the throat, and do not put heat on it except for a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After they do another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cauteries be which are called "clavicle" from which we have the shape in front;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure the limb as we have said before until it be healthy.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When the tumor and illness of the lung are from cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or cough, and the illness is ancient, then apply two cauterizations on the ribs in the affected places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cauterization between the two breasts in the chest;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cauterization be that which is called "clavicle" according to the shape that was previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, apply cauterization by pricking all of the cauterization that is called "points" because of the shape which was previously described in the illness of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be thirty, or as many as needed.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing the back according to what was previously said, and let the cauterization be at three ribs according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And therefore are the cauterings less severe, because you make three at one time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards the patient feels better on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after lift the heart that is within the tickled area of your left hand fingers;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the cauterization which has two nerves where it is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart as long as it penetrates to the side, and comes the figure of the cauterization together with four cauterizations;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason the cautery is made with the cautery that has III nerves, because the figure of cauterization is thus six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a thread and it's the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve, because it has eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Afterwards put on the cautery rough threads with wax;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after make the patient rest, and not move the limbs by long tension until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, little matter what happens next, then make a cautery on the thickness of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is re-formed, and the moisture is stopped and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach there come chills and many humors as it withdraws from its complexion, and are multiplied the cathars to it, and in manners of accustomed cures and it does not profit at all, then it is necessary that the patient be warmed on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Of this have made three cauteries on the buttocks for the quantity of an egg, and all the cautery is placed, and two cauteries under the two ribs as many as the figure of the cauteries will be at three angles, and let there be space between one and another so that they are not joined together when they will suppurate;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cautery be so deep that it pierces the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a cautery of a large cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cautery, let the cautery be applied by pricking and marking on the stomach at the point according to the quantity that you see of the weakness;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then apply the cautery to all the areas which are called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we had before, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When to the liver comes pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is excessively mixed out of its natural composition by the superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated for what we have said in sections, and it does not profit him, thus it is necessary that the patient be warmed on his liver;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark the weakness with three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, below the hypochondries, where the pain or the ache of the stomach comes;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and have a space between each cautery the thickness of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cautery be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too much on the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it be burned just enough to cauterize the heart, and let the patient stand upright on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then let him sit, and stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauteries of the cutaneous layer, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the whole heart, for you would dry out the entire body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not come near to the navel, for the heart is very subtle in that place, and one must be cautious to see;
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too severe;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels a very sharp pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment of the abscesses is done, it is necessary that the patient be supported on his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark from below the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a razor, whose form is this:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize the cautery until the flesh is burned, and come up to the sphincter, until the pourette is entirely purified;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of the sores as long as it is healthy;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not necessary that anyone use this cautery except those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these diseases have been cured many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then it can hardly work, and yet it seems to me that moving is better than letting it be.
