dou cautere de pleuresin	against the cauterization of the pleura
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The old ones said that one should do to the pleura cauterizations of roots of aristolochia, and in such manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristolochia as long, the largest that you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and put it in oil, and dip it in fire, and cauterize the cauterization between the shoulder and the neck, and make two small cauterizations slightly descending on the part that is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and make two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a little backwards;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cauterization in the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest opposite the cauterization which is between the shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but make an opening as with an aromatic.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancient ones said that no man should use the fire cauterization on the razor and warm it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess;
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and the pain would cease, as we have said concerning the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient will die now, or a fistula will come which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the bladder
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the bladder according to what we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not benefit him, then they apply three kinds of cauterization that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	One manner is that you make three or four cauterizations, burning according to the length of the bladder, according to the shape of the liver cauterization that we have spoken of before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be seated behind his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and raise the heart which is near the thigh, where the pain of the patient comes from the left side, and let the elevation that you raise the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After that, burn the two nerves inflamed until the heart is perceived from the other side, and then withdraw the cautery, and thus in it will have four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see that, cauterize the entire cautery on three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when he has obtained purification by long stretching, and it is better than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not suitable for dropsical people, except in the manner which is called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat according to the methods that we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit them, then it is necessary that you do four cauteries around the navel, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one on the right side of the chest.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the cauteries be well pressed near the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After leaving the cautery open to obtain purification by long stretching, and do not abandon the treatment of the disease after the cautery;
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will come together with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cautery for the belly is the spoon that we have shown before.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been previously described.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and full of watery citrine, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and the anular;
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and raise your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep, lest the watery citrine be stirred up, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After that, make on each leg two cauteries at the point of the cuticle.
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauterizations of the thigh be one side of the knee in front and the other behind, on the leg;
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauterizations exposed for a long time without dressing, until they heal;
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of other treatments that we have spoken of.
de la menoison	of the dislocation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a disorder of the stomach comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by methods of treatments;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong virtue, then perform a large cauterization on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before about the cauterization of the stomach, with circular cauterization;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and 4 subtle cauterizations around the navel to each subtle clavicle cauterization, and 2 cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, have them cauterized on the finger, and have the cautery on each nail, and have two small cauteries on the stomach below the great, for the treatment is profitable when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or one or several, and are old and are of thick cold and moist humors corrupted, and are curable as we have said in sections, and it does not profit at all, make a cautery:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	Three on the spine of the back, which is entirely divided into sections, little by little in a triangular shape, and make one cautery under the navel, and two on the buttocks;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the food does not digest, and one sees the face swell, then have a large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cauteries of the clave;
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the cauterized area stay stretched tight.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure, leave it alone as long as it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the skin condition known as "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut into the thelul, if you warm up the cauterized iron that seems to ease it, and then apply it all wrapped up onto the cut thelul;
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and let your hand be so that the cauterization comes to the birth of the vein, from which the blood flows out;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do it one or two times, and if there is a lot of thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the treatment of profitable joints as long as they are healthy;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cauterizer on the achates, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly healed
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure surgery or cauterization, which we will relate in its place, then comes a disease that cannot be healed unless by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is an abnormal growth of a fistula, and it is inflamed and infected with rotten and corrupted matter, then the doctor must test all around with a subtle probe, and take care to know all around how deep the probe goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cauterizer which seems to be at a comfortable temperature, and thrust it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and reapply the cauterizer as long as those rotten and corrupted parts are burned, one time, or two, or three, according to the quantity of their need.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and beware of the nerves that are irritated, and of the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestines, beware of these places, and do not make those false passages that are in the body of the charcoal, and think that it is not a perforating thing;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After the cure, the body is healthy as long as it is sound, and if the places are healed, and the materials are pulled for a long time, then they are dry, that the body is entirely healthy;
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	and if the materials are not pulled, it means that the body is hoarse and rotten, and the bone is corrupted at the source;
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and thus like one of those things that we will tell about in his body.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys, and of great swelling, and does not take a woman's temperament, then it is necessary that you do cauterization on the kidneys on one side and on the other with the cauterizing iron that we have previously mentioned;
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	and if we apply the cauterizations to the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and they will be of greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is weak and chilly from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then apply cautery to the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, on the right and left, and let each cautery be as long as a finger;
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and have one cautery on the back, or two if you are in a bind;
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	and let the cauteries be fixed according to the previously described form.
de la marris	of the thigh
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the thigh is cold and moist, and does not allow for it to conceive because of this, and the flesh is corrupted and its limits are delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, they feel great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is necessary to perform three cauterizations around the belly, as we have said regarding the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauterizations be done with a key, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the thigh
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous humors descend to the box of the thigh, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and the places of separation are found, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the box of the thigh with a cauterization similar to a circle, and mark in front of the place around the box as it turns, so that the box is within the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and if there are cauteries such as those for which one cauterizes the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if there are no cauteries present, then make three cauteries of the large olive tree, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the abscesses;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal them until they are healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the thigh
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the thigh, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the section and the cure is not effective, and the illness is chronic:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick foul humors with fetid pills, or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After you make a cauterization;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the method of cauterizing is according to two methods:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	It is to know assemblage of burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, of which one is thus:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the box of the flanks three triangular cauteries in this form, and make a deep and large hole, and let there be between each cauterization the thickness of an egg, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	sometimes one does a cauterization in the middle of the head of the flanks, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see that it is cauterized with a circular cauterization that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the flanks;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but make it in such a way that the circles contain the entire flank, and all the spaces of the heart be dry.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method one uses for sciatica, when the pain is in the thigh, and does not reach just to the knee nor just to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it reaches the knee and the leg, have two cauteries made there where the patient says the pain is, and one cauterization above the ankle four fingers, on the left side a little;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cauteries be shallow, and let the thickness of the scar be according to the curvature;
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers or near the navel, then cauterize there where he feels the pain three points or four at the cauterization which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it is necessary, have more made;
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, have a cauterization made with a shallow or circular cauterization, and take great care in all your cauteries that you not leave so much of the cauterization that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have performed cauterization on the leg near the foot, and they let it go so long that the leg became totally swollen, and the foot also, and was pierced and corrupted to the bottom of the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a bowel movement from which he got death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, perform cauterization on one and on the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise men said in the cauterization of the thigh, that this is the method, make an iron instrument and let it be as thick as a small nut or a little less, and let it be hollow and the space from one hollow to the other be the size of a walnut.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the hollows be open on two sides, and also be like nuts, and have an iron handle well made;
et c’est li forme:	and it is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And let it be heated until it is entirely red and hot to the touch, and then apply it to the affected side of the patient's thigh, and turn on the healthy side of the body;
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and let the cautery be applied once, and the dressing remain for three days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a plaster of butter, and let the wound be covered with it for a long time;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of the shoulder until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly because of its danger, and few see those who use it;
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless this is one of the good cauteries, which one can suffer, and where it adheres to.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The medical cauterizing instrument is such that you make between the joints an instrument in which descends the margin of the door, and it should be of copper or iron with a long blade, and in height it has two nuts, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a finger;
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and are open upwards and downwards, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	Afterwards place on the box of the thigh to the patient gazing upon his healthy side, and press your hand much on the box of the thigh;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	afterwards put between the two circles of the warm water which has been heated by the fire a little, and let it for an hour or ten, and let the patient suffer from the heat and the burning of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there is found mortification as if from fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the mortifications have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the thigh of warm water, and let it be for three hours, and put on a poultice as long as what is black from the eschar remains;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let it remain for three hours that the rotting is in a strap;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last aid after the treatment of ouching parts as long as it is healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, have made the instrument that holds according to what you have done on the same side of the hip;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the manner of the warm water, and I have written it in the treatise of the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and living lime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	or it should have a small hole there so that the point of a needle can enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put that pot in another pot well plugged, and put on it the alkaline and lime and sweet water, as much as there should be two fingers of the powders when you have well pressed with your hand;
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let it be so until it descends into the water and takes hold of a cup or a lead weight, then take all that water, and cast it on hot coals and on quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in many works of medicine and in cauterizations of other limbs.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it does work like fire, and also other medicines that one cauterizes well the thigh thus with thesis and myrrh and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure in which a man was cured of the pain of the thigh and of the sciatic vein, and praised it much, and said that no other cure was made, and that he was healthy at once when this cure was done, and he had bathed as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And it is applied in a manner that you press green fresh and dry litharge, and you bruise it much with a piece of fat, and put it on the thigh and on the thigh muscle and on the leg where the pain is, and the injury;
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and let it be for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath until the body is somewhat warmed, and make him enter into bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healthy.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And be aware that one should not use cauterization of such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a fig leaf, it helps much;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and the cauterization should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take the wool and the fat of old oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb of the foot and the other called the heel.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	Take dry fibers of goat's kidney, and dip them in fire until they are charcoal, and then put them on the wool, and let it be until it is stained.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and do it again thus, and do not cease to do it thus until you think by sensation that it comes near the skin, and that the pain is eased;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this manner of cauterization is called "cauterization of the goat".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from a blow or from percussion or from excessive evacuation, or from similar matters of cold and spread material, none of these things is worthy of cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after this that the patient is freed from foul-smelling pills or similar things, that one applies to their back, where the pain is, three signed lines of enchantment, and in each line a cautery or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cautery be made according to the cautery that is called "branding";
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see fit, make three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this disease comes to little children, and the signs of the affliction are that they have a constricted arm when they lift it, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you will find in the upper part of the spine of the back and in the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, then cauterize it with a cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cautery takes hold of each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a cautery that pricks two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, anoint the limb until it be healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery in angularity which is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pain of the joints is caused by moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the physicians properly call "podagra", and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in such manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a swelling that you prick on the face of the foot, then make a cauterization at the entire spot where one calls «point».
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come near the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make a cauterization on each knee three or four cauterizations of each part, all olive-shaped;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you are a master of more, if you make more, but do not hold your hand further than until the expectation of the heart is dry.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then administer the cauterization that we have spoken of in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks around the forearm two lines;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if it remains a point of pain at the elbow, then make punctures on each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come near the skin or near the muscles, then cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and think of medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good governance for him and you purge his phlegm, then he will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes to the entrails, and the bowels descend to the groin and it is a novelty, then it is necessary that when you cure the wound, he does not urinate that day;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he uses things that loosen the stomach, so that the flatus descends from his stomach;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his belly as long as the bowels are being repaired, and apply them to your fingers, and anoint with oil under the rupture on the bone of the hip, and put a sign that is similar to half a circle above the navel;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then apply the cautery to the place where the form is
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and throws out tendons.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then put back the intestines in their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and let the assistants hold their hands on them so they do not turn back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and open well the thighs of the patient, and put one cushion and one sheet on the thighs, and another on the chest who holds the hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then start again another time until you come to the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and take care subtly that the intestine does not protrude when you perform the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that because of this the patient does not die, or other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauterizations of children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and of large people also large according to their measure;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days cure the limb from the cautery of butter until the scab is formed;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the cure of other ulcers until it be healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well dried;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his bandages be tied loosely, so that the belly does not protrude when he goes to the chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let a well-made poultice be applied to him, and for forty other days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let it have good rest, so that it works little and guards against too great a repletion of drinking and eating, and of too high a breath;
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when it makes this teaching then it is entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will speak after the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ruptures come in other bellies and are connected, and you see that they do not grow anymore, have it cauterized with a cauterization iron according to its quantity, and let the third of the heart be scarred;
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that one should be cauterized with a cauterizer at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the wound and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold in hand the entire cauterizing iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of pain in an old member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any member, from a fall or from a blow, and this pain lasts a long time, and the treatment with medicine is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins", and let the cautery be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its strength and its location of torsions and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if it is healed from the first cauterization, that's good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if this does not work, recommend another cauterization on that one, for such is the custom that it must be changed in the member that is closest to it, because it is necessary that you do the cauterizations as long as the patient is not healed.
de meselerie	Of mixture
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mixtures are aided sometimes by cauterization with great help, and also the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you wish to cauterize, beware that the illness is at its beginning, and if it is curable according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen nor deteriorate, and you doubt that the corruption will not infect the whole disease, then make a cauterization on the head.
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	Put one end at the nape of the neck, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and two on the temples, and one behind on the occiput;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and let it be so that the cauterization reaches just to the bone, and as long as the crusts come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can exit;
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and the cautery on the mouse according to what is before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the mixture is scattered all around;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it does manifestly, then you must apply the cautery of these cauteries that we have spoken of in the head, and one cautery on the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the thorax and another below, and two on the shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and of the feet, and on the palms of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are on the rear calf, that you not burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the fist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And you should know that the more I do of cauterization, the more I do to help, and it brings him profit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and you should know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cauterization as much as they feel it, because their body is already totally corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manners of the cases.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, treat the wound with flour of wheat with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When inflammation comes to any limb and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauterizations on the limb according to its size and smallness.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauterization be a little deep into the thickness of the skin;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the joints as long as they are healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And sometimes one performs cauterization on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is a bone that has become inflamed;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and however does not interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of paralysis
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "paralysis" has taken hold, and the instruments of medicine are of no use, then cauterize with a cauter a little deeply, according to the quantity of the thickness of the chest, until the flesh is burned and its color is changed;
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then heal with a paste made from breadcrumbs and lentils mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of dove and blood of swallow, taking each a part;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be mixed all together, and let it be tied with a cloth, and let it be hung on the leg as long as it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer first appears, and you want to stop it, then cauterize with a cauterizing iron which seems to encircle, all around the tumor of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And the wise men said that one should make a cauterization in the middle of the cancer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and yet it does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen many times;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and a more proper thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cauterizing iron that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When some people have an illness called "adubelati", and it slows down movement or because of the excess that it creates or because of the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you hasten the stoppage of movement:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then you cauterize around a lot of small cauters by pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	after that, leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it hastens to stop moving.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through the entire cauter, then heat the cauter of the material that is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that illness which is called "adubelati" until the cauters have pierced the heart, and let the cauters be such that the patient feels relief in some manner so that the course of the corruption is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire by means of iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness is what is called "corrosive" disease, and it is nothing other than a wound to a limb, for it eats away the limbs just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this disease in someone who can suffer cauterization with fire together, then heat the cauterizing irons very small and large, according to what is needed for the person or where the disease is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After the cauterization of all parts, as long as you eradicate all the corruption, and none of it remains, that all that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and apply to the cauterized limbs a soothing balm with oil, until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of painful wounds, there is generated heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see that after three days healthy flesh does not grow, it's a good sign;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if it does not, then reapply the cautery to that which remains corrupted of the limbs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this treatment has often been cured by sharp medicine instead of cautery of fire;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but nevertheless the cautery of fire is of greater aid, and I have already spoken of the treatment with sharp medicine in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take the quantity that you need for your craft.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that to the feet by default is born a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and is a gross faulty thing that afflicts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is known as cauterization by fire, and cauterization by hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Cauterization by fire is that you heat the cauterizing iron as if it were a pen of wool, and let it be made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the nail on all sides, and that it has subtle edges;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	Afterwards, place all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let it stay thus three hours until it induces the beginning of suppuration;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a plaster of crushed wild mallows mixed with oil, and let the plaster stay on all night, and the nail will fall out and be disrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the joint by anointing with warmth as long as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are affected by various sores on the body, and often occur in the hands and feet, then you should apply cauterization with warm water;
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in a similar manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a chain of iron or a bar of steel, and put it on the nail and the elbow, that is to say for removing warts;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and put the chain on it so that it embraces all around, then you put a little warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand turning it so that the margin of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and then find the warm water penetrating just to the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient suffer a little the burning of the warm water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then let it be, and it will tear out everything with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this after another, as long as you extract all those that are in the body, then cure the unctions which cause the fever.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some tremble with cold or with nerves, or with quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you do four cauterizations or four on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each vertebra;
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cauterization on the foot, and one on the stomach with olive cauterization;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	it will stop the trembling, and hasten the health from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	of boils that produce pus
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear through the skin ulcers, or boils that produce pus, which come from corrupted thick matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	If it is necessary first when they appear to make a cauterization on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cauterization with the nest of a dead tree worm, from which the point is taken to be seared by fire, or from the root of long aristolochia, or with the lens-shaped cauterizer.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow in front, but are broken up the excesses from which they come, and are made healthy;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great outpourings of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very grievous thing to dislocate
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And however when it happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your second finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very firmly until the blood is stilled beneath your finger, and so that nothing more comes out;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then apply to the fire the olive cauteries, many small and large ones as long as they are quite red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take I, either large or small according to the wound and the limb in which the artery is cut, and apply the cautery on that vein where you hold with your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it should flow when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is stemmed;
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and beware that you do not injure the nerve that is nearby, and that another evil does not come to the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and be aware that when one is deprived of the skill of an artery, one cannot well restrain it especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four methods that we have mentioned:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treatable, or by a strong tightening of a thread, or by medications applied which have the power to restrain blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and let it be bound and constrained firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	For one who administers a tight binding of dressings or of putting hot things on, or other similar things, it is of little profit if not done properly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if it happens to anyone and he does not have a doctor or medicine present, then he should put his finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it is restrained both above the wound and above the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move the joint, but rather apply cold moisture often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stiffened;
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make inquiries beforehand about those things for which there is need of cauterizations and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	In this book, the second part concerns the treatments for stone disease.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease for which it is suitable to apply a fire cauterization, or a hot medicine, and the organs and the causes and the humors and the forms of the cauterizations;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have placed that chapter concerning the head down to the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method for what one finds more easily what one desires.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin with this, it is necessary, dear reader, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one concerning cauterizations, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you do not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for a cure.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if there come those who so aggravate themselves with their disease that they die easily because of the force of the treatment that they receive for their disease, and from the greatness of their evil;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And to those who give their opinion, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	wait, I am ready";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is contemptible.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It does not matter to you that you are seen by those who come to you with this condition, but put greater concern in your honor than in your gain, and do not open foolishly but wisely about the things of which you are certain, and of which you can have taken and profits.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter for you by dividing it into chapters, according to what it is before the chapter on cauterizations, which I have divided for you from head to feet, so that you find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Head full of pus
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	It is known that this disease often occurs in infants due to the nurse holding the infant's head too tightly;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it happens for a hidden reason that one is not aware of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this disease except in infants, and most of those that I have seen died quickly.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me that it is better for me to omit the work in some treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw an infant whose head was full of pus, and the head became so swollen each day that it could not be supported;
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture increased so much that it became a tumor, and this tumor is gathered beneath the bone on the spine, between the heart and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the work is such that if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make in the head a large incision;
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and let it be as long as two of us, until the moisture runs;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see to it the form of a spatula;
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see the sutures of the head opened on each side, and the water jumps up when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not seem to be an answer:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it is necessary that you make in the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract the moisture entirely from outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After constricting the fissures of bandages and powders, and put wine and oil, and let it be like that until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then undo it, and treat the wound with dressings and with ointments, and let the head of the diseased limb be constricted, and give to eat to the patient dry victuals of little moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another method of incising is that you look at the extent of the abscess, and the gathering of the pus;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for sometimes it is in front;
aucune fois derrier;	sometimes behind;
aucune fois en destre;	sometimes on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Cut then the place where the abscess is open, and the filling of the pus, and make the incision according to that which you have the power;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and let flow a little blood, so that the patient dies from lack of blood and from evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is a certain disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the chest, and the disease is chronic, and the treatment with medicine is of no benefit, then the last resort for a cure is cauterization with what one cuts the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is necessary then, when you cut the veins, that the patient makes his head recline;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after rubbing the limb with a rough cloth so that the arteries appear, then the patient tightens his neck against the whole cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look where the vein beats, and the limbs on one side and the other are behind the ears, and are a little relaxed;
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then sign the limbs of the enclosure, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula on both sides, as long as the tail vein goes to the bone, and that which is by the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, remove the spatula from beneath the artery and cut above, carving just as the two veins across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then the blood jumps up continually outside.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not appear on feeling, then it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign the enclosure and make it go to the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and that which is necessary to put blood outside if it is six scruples, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the replenishment of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	then examine the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains on the bone at the pointed edge of the shin, if the pus does not come from the abscess, then strain the wound and bind it, and the treatment of the application as long as it is not healthy.
de emigrainne	of migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migration comes, and sharp catarrh, for the moisture of tears and the heat in temples and old chronic weakness and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and all that does not profit him, then let us cauterize the arteries of the temples and the cautery.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the way of extraction is that the patient makes to grow the hairs on his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little pushed further than in some men who are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is put back, then remove the patient's neck from some cloths, then rub the limb with a coarse cloth, and wrap the limb in warm clothes as long as the artery appears manifestly;
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula of which is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then scratch the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then pull it high with pincers, and separate it well from the tissues that are joined to each part;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is subtle, then turn it to the point of the nail, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then the blood does not cease at all in any way.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And let out blood of the sixth degree, up to the third;
