En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case then of these thick skins which is thin and not encrusted, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open their nostrils, and cut the ligament at those thick skins, and pull them strongly;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then consider that you must support the subtle sharp point of the spatula on one side, as long as you know that the instrument is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, then open it to all the subtle and lightweight instruments, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and let it heal without suppression, or a hot abscess, if you drain it as is necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize the wound as much as the blood is stagnant and all the flesh is hardened, then anoint with oil or vinegar and sharp wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wounds open, and discharge comes to the palate, know that it is a sign of health;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if discharge does not pass as it should, know that there is dead flesh in the hollow bone, because the instruments do not come to cut through;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then it is necessary that you put on a thread of linen, somewhat thick, and let it be known by us, and have between each knot a space of two fingers or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's head on the thread in his nostril to smell it, and pull it in pulling so that it comes through the nostril inside the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times they do this to the child as a trick, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the end which comes through the nostril in one hand, and the other end which comes through the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other being careful of us who are on the thread;
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do it as long as you know that the knots have pressed on that flesh, then pull the threads, suck the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the nostrils as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Make this for three days or more, as long as the ligaments corrode all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on a plaster of pounded leaves for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for dry medicines, then use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills the oils and the medicines;
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And let it be of silver or of brass, similar to a covered lamp, like a chain, and the conductor thus;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, then make a closed chain, and let the instruments be flat to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle at the top to hold it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a growth appears on the head near the nose, a disease which is called "telul", and grows and increases greatly, until it is a visible thing to behold;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason it is necessary that you cut at the beginning, and remove all dead tissue, then apply the cautery or the burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if it is necessary to cauterize so that it becomes large, take heed if it is hard, of dark color, of little sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you do not touch it with iron, for that is an infected abscess, because when one cuts into it, great evil comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that one can cut into it, then warn the patient and cut with caution, and treat the area with drying and constricting remedies.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and wounded
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Be aware that when a flow of discharge comes from one of these wounded cartilages, it benefits little, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary then when it happens to anyone, if one examines whether the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then joins the two lips of a wound to a seam, then cures it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you cauterize all the parts of the wound until they heal, then assemble the two lips into a seam, and constrict it, and powder with powder of blood of dragon, and incense bruised;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of Paris or another plaster that sticks, and let it be until it adheres by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healed;
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of the wound closure is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the closure of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	To hands men have we within the lips an aposteme hard, similar to grains of seeds, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you pierce the lips, and split into each knot, and take it with pincers and cut in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then put in the brain after the incision of vitriol broth, until the blood is stanched;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the liver of arsenic, and treat the brain with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there grows on the gums a fleshy growth joined, which the old call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let flow the pus or the blood;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the limb a vitriolic broth, or other powders that are restrictive and drying;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the wound reopens after the incision, and often happens, so that a second time it scabs over, and is cauterized:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not reopen after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the scabs for covering.
des sordens	of abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they gather at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and worm-eaten, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth is stinking;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if it is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and you take the teeth or the scabs appearing, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make from the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, as long as they are removed;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes that which is in the first layer, it's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything resolved;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the tooth has need of various shapes of instruments to scrape, according to what the work demands, because the roots that one scrapes from the teeth have other forms than those that one scrapes between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and let these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay as long as you can, because one should not do harm;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it's a very noble substance, thus one has no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained by a pulling instrument, it is necessary that you are certain of the teeth that are causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and causes pulling of the bad tooth;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not depart from that place, as long as the bad tooth is extracted, for we have already seen it happen to these wise men;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the tooth that is causing pain, it is necessary that you scratch around the tooth with all a strong spatulum to guard the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then put your fingers or subtle pincers at the first poke and poke, until it is well loosened, then firmly grip the pincers;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be in your healthy hand between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part, and move it as you have done previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is decayed and rotten, then it is necessary to fill it with cloths, where the gaps are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you extract it subtly with pincers, so that it does not break while extracting;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to be very careful in working around the gum to avoid dislodging the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And it is good to warn that you should not break it, and leave a part behind, and cause the patient, by the wickedness of the root, greater pain than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons, who through their hastiness and hardness sometimes break the instrument, and do not heed what we have stated;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but they come sometimes from the questioning of that great sickness for the roots that remain there, or from the cartilage that it breaks, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is extracted, then wash the place with wine or vinegar and soap;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if an effusion of blood comes, which often happens, then fill the place with a mixture of vitriol and broth;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that is not enough, then cauterize it;
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shape of the instruments, for which one removes the teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and should be made of well-finished iron, and should have teeth to hold the grip.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the socket, it is necessary that you put on the spot a moist cotton cloth for one or two hours, until the gums are softened, then you extract the teeth which are called "algefri", because of the pain.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they are made dense like a file and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these instruments, it is necessary that you discover the flesh entirely around the root, and you put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a pelican, because of this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and large so that it does not break the tooth, and if the root jumps out by itself, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if it does not, then you aid with all the instruments, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one aids oneself with this instrument which has two arms, from which its form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front for the purpose of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, from which its form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many tooth-instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not mentioned;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach the use of an instrument due to the diversity of ills and if it breaks or shatters the cartilage or other bones, or if it decays, then one seeks the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and aids oneself with gestures, from which its form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-held to hold the bone, so it does not shatter, but can be held and extracted;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb with suitable medicines for that, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, thus the remedy is for all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with the natural body, and their form is ugly, and especially in women, it happens that you know if the teeth are newborn after the tooth, and not in the right place, and one cannot chew or file them:
adonques lou raie;	then the rasping tool;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is rough with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is thus, and resembles a small beak, and let it be of sharpened iron at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut a little and a little with the forceps in the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then the file of one part files as its form is:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is like the file with which one makes the needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in filing the tooth little by little and lightly with gentle touches, so that it does not move until it is steady;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the surface at the end of any roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bites the tongue, then you must file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth aches, either from percussion or from cold, and the patient cannot press on it because it hurts, and you try to treat them with astringent medicines, but that is not effective;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then you must hold it with a thread of gold, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold does not change;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to thread the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the thread between the diseased teeth, if there is one or several, until you come wisely just to the other healthy tooth;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then bring the covering close to the part where you started, and pull your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the ends of the thread to one knot, and gather them, and pass them behind the healthy tooth, and put it so that it does not bite the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone, or the thread breaks, then constrain it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains and serves thus all its tension, and it is the form of the teeth and the alignment of the upper teeth and the lower teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one interfere who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes makes the form of a tooth from the bone of a cow, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and holds it as we have said, and remains and serves thus for long tension.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes there is a ligament that comes from the teeth to the tongue by nature, which one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or from an accidental wound under the palate;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your teeth, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then cut the nervous vein broadly, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if it has hardness or swelling, and it is a sudden wound, then anoint the unguent and cut broadly that which holds.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is exposed;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done, raise the leg of water of hot or cold, then put under the tongue a piece of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and bind the patient every night, so that the legs cannot swell.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, then put on the leg vitriol broth;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with a gentle cautery, which is good for that;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat with another treatment until it is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a black or dark colored fistula, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it declines to the bladder, and there is moisture, then he throws the stone, and makes a subtle spatula, and delivers from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if his blood fails in your work, then put on a warm broth as long as it is strained, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from the axle and from the seat, and treat other treatments until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	A tumor sometimes comes inside the throat called "godath", and we properly call them the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the section, and they are not healthy, take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is a hard abscess with little sensation and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and its root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of the evacuation of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will cut it, where it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and rounded, and its root is subtle, prepare the instrument for cutting, but first check if the abscess is warm and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in the sun, and his hands be on your lap, and open his mouth and hold his tongue between your hands, and press it down to the bottom of the instrument, according to its shape;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or subtle copper, as thin as a knife;
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue against this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the nail and insert it in the handle, and pull it forcibly upwards more than you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull something from the tiles with it, then fit it to the instrument, of which this is the form, that seems like a strong force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all of it is curved, and one part to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then fit it to the tenailles, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be sharp on one side, and named on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have fitted one of the handles, then fit the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and with warm and running, and if there is discharge of blood, then gargle the patient, or cooked pomades of green plants, or fumigations of myrrh, and similar things, until the wound is stanched;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then leave the treatment until he is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes there appear in the throat other abscesses than the two tonsils, if one cuts them then thus like the two tonsils equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed inside her throat, that is to say the abscess of the uvula;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had already well pressed close the whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had stayed thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was already so grown that it had put out two roots through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then as much as possible, and fixed in one of the angles, then pulled out the trachea, and with it a large portion of the throat.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I healed another part in the other wound of the nose, and I opened the mouth and I pressed the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After that I pierced the abscess, and I drained a part of it, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and then the throat of the woman was cleared, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting into that abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses repeatedly grew back, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I inserted and cauterized it within the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from those parts, and knew not what God did after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the humors descend to the womb, and it is inflated and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is unevenly thick and round, then it is called "womb".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is purified as we have said in the section, and the purification does not benefit it, and you see that the ulcerous abscesses are appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is round, gathered and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a dark brown color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then fix the ankle in the hole, and pull it straight, and cut with the instrument of the two humors that I mentioned in the incision of the two arms.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not remove more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two arms, and treat it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear to be cut, then it is necessary that you use caution in the cauterization of the sensitive area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp pointed.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and constricts it with a sharp pointed iron, so that it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in the handling of this instrument, from which its shape is formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let the head have a dressing where the medicine is applied, just like the handling of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine on the egg;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be sitting on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth with the medicine inside, so it does not go down the throat, and to the bladder;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the egg, for a quarter of an hour, until you see it becoming numb and the bites of the medicine are alleviated;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and envelop it in an instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton in the chain above, until the cotton adheres to the egg;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, as long as the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and apply a plaster after 4 days or 5.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have the skill of reintroducing the cautery of the medicine, then reintroduce it, and after the cautery apply a dressing around the wound, made with cotton padded in butter, and cleanse that which is around the affected area;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be treated with cold water, and let it be cured of gargling as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than the incision, nor the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calament and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and aloe and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in one pot, and add oil, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well stuck in strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there is the instrument which is shaved in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or of lead, and one of the pieces should be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise to the eye through the vein, until the eye is deadened;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the remedy is often repeated, until the eye is dry, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the emergence of the hot abscess, for many things happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do it near to the declination of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, then take a reed and put in the end of it a piece of wool, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the claw of a bird does not touch the greasy steam on the mouth, and it is a good cure for salvation together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it rises to the throat bone or spine of fish, or similar things;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	if it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sole of the foot with all the instrument, so that you see the thing moved;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear and is thrown back into the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cut in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance the thing comes out through the vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of flax, or a root of lettuce, or a crust of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie to the sponge a thread, and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, if it is rough, then you will rub forcibly;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take the instrument of plaster according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the curved instruments be at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head held high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of it comes out, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is good that the patient himself puts in the instrument, because he knows better or the thing is rough;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if he puts it in downwards, or he pulls it forcibly with all the instrument equally, as long as it is downwards.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the soreness of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Certain times the soreness is treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when that does not benefit the patient, then examine the throat in the sunlight, then press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood vessel, treat it with a small needle, or with subtle pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not effective, take a heated needle, and insert it in the patient's throat, then blow or expel the humors of the needle with hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever the whole day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full handful of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in such a way as to swallow, and move it with the hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if you feel that the blood vessel is in the throat, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not gush out as we have said, then suffocate the patient with assafoetida, through the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the uva.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will pour out without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of the fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are hot coals, and it be covered with a perforated cloth, and in this pierced one put the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you give the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes just to the nose;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the nose will discharge now, and if it does not gush out, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, and has bitter and salty things, and does not drink anything watery;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and therefore it is necessary that it be removed by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument for which one draws the blood, is, when one can see it, similar to curved tongs for entering into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has resemblance to a hawk's beak, and it has roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot release;
et vez ci la forme:	and see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what the memory recalls here after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and in cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways of which one is in its own likeness itself, and from what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs where they are attached to the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come in the joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if it is an abscess that one should not pierce, as long as the belly is swollen according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if it is one of those that needs to be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets them be until they are purulent outside, then by chance the ligament and the nerve of the joint become corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is near a principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it becomes swollen, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Where it is deep in the foundation, then pierce with anise so that it dies;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is necessary that you pierce the abscess with completed digestion, unless it is deep in the foundation, so that it does not putrefy within, and be cleaned inside, and a fistula comes;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the work of perforation of the abscess which dies according to completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and of the redness, and the abatement and the soothing of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the perforation or that which depends on the place of the abscess, and where it appears dead;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let there be a perforation of the length of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or the feet, or in the joints and in the kidneys and in the arteries, and in all equal places where there is no place of plethora.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that swell, according to which member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce before that, you will release the venom from him, and it is full of a lot of filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they penetrate the lips and his innermost depths.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to that which the member has need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you make small incisions, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large wounds, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the head, and cauterize;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become numb like the fingers, and is numbnessed, then one must do it as one does for the buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such that are cut into three angles, and if there are such that one cuts just like the edge of a knife, just like abscesses of the entrails;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cauterizations.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, not to drain all the pus at once, but to drain a part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just short of the other eye, then touch some thing straight away;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	make that by many times of bone to bone, until the arm is entirely dislocated;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the vein often bursts with the issue of the arm, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Avoid then this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is large, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a flat incision, then apply bandages of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put on each one a bandage so that they come one against the other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, then it is necessary that you fill it with a warm poultice or with a dressing of flax or linen threads moistened.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then anoint the bone, and treat the joint until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is a flow of blood in your work, apply a cold and easy bandage, and moisten the cloth, and put it on the wound flowing many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the flow of blood persists, apply a treatment and cure, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book on the wounds, and if it is in the time of winter, and the wound or abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and moist cloths soaked in wine and hot oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the limbs are fleshy, then you must apply moist dressings in water and in oil, or in wine and in cold oil, until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess and the cyst and treat it, as it is necessary, until it becomes healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is necessary to know universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have already told you how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and see it in this chapter.
des soros	of the sores (or ulcers)
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and are types of tumors that are in the thighs, as well as the joint of a knee, and many have similar characteristics.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There is fat and such things where there is moisture, like in pouces;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are those that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no point of doubt, then one should not do the opposite.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the tailor is such that you examine all the instrument called "intermissive", from which its form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they make it with two pieces of wood.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, then one scrapes without leaving anything the skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves nothing;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, with vinegar and with oil, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who run will be those who remain from nothing.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then touch the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain a single knot.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound of the shoulder joint with suitable remedies, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscesses have a fatty tumor, cut according to this form, from the length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cut your scalpels, and scrape all around, and put all your treatment of drawing on the coat where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery is made contrary, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do with the abscess if it is pierced, and of cutting and of curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the pierced abscess and the moist place, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if to some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and of these abscesses that I treated on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had touched it with a needle, one would have made a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming on the head, there are those that appear on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening is such that it should be touched daily, depending on the condition, to allow the pus to flow out;
et les cure si com il covient.	and the treatment as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofula disease
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the shoulders, and in the corners, and sometimes appear in other parts of the body, and are numerous, and are joined one to another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly inside its coat, as with the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not harsh with the nerves of the neck nor in the artery nor in the channel, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scratch each part, and the two lips of the wound are like onions, if you are skilled, as we have said in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and cut a little and a little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and it is not necessary for the spatula to be too sharp, so the hands are not tired, and do not go too far, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and that does not stop the bleeding, then put on the wound a vitriol broth, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound steady;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then look at your hand to see if there remain small scrofula, and cut them and cure them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is in the root of the scrofula a large vein, it is not necessary that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by itself, without harming;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then apply the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there was no remaining surplus due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cut out the root of it, and pull out strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that have a surplus, pierce them there where it appears most prominent;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and prick them thus as was said beforehand, in dependence, then I will apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts that which remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then apply a cure of ointment and anointing with charm, until it is healthy.
de squinance	of friction
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancient ones spoke and talked about the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have a stammer, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cleaned;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one should not trust this remedy, because all the veins and the body of the patient with abscess are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the body, it is necessary to operate on the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we make a small incision of about three circles or four, a little cutting across, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cutting of the skin, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those veins are found at the section of the diaphragm such that there is no junction of flesh, and the vessels are long with anguish.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the muscles are swollen, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to its full length, then cuts the chest as far as it comes to the clavicle;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and search for the blood vessels, if you see any thing, and then cut the tissue, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is shown by the section of the flesh of the clavicle that the blood flows through the limb which is broken, and by the deficiency of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound covered with a dressing.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed from which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the chest, and sew it gently without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that make hair grow, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Do not give this treatment unless the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient appears to be near death, and the defect is in the spleen or the gut.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and because of this the old man commands to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or in four; And then he commands to sew the wound and to treat, until it is cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the sinews of the lung from the breast;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the healer, and I found him as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and it was good that it had not taken a course through the vein or the throat, and the veins were issuing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and did not have to the lady outside of where she had been rough in voice, and returned afterwards to her appearance;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I said that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no pain.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "strangury of the throat", and is a large abscess in the colour of a jasmine, and is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	Natures, and accidents;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural does not have a point of intelligence.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to two manners, one of which is similar to a crisis for us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it causes fear, and it is not suitable to perform cauterization except in cases where it is small, and one proves and examines throughout the entire interior.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you thrust it as with a blunt instrument, and do not penetrate to any vein, then you cut, just as one cuts the nails, and you treat all its substance, if there is a point to it;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everywhere, and cure it as it requires, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of the nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of nails, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it happens that I see all the difference that is between swelling and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that discharge is heat and fever holding, as long as the abscess has passed, and it is accompanied by decay;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and the heat are relieved.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the swelling there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a thick fluid, which is its own special humor, and is according to the color of the body, and increases like a tumor, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two similarities, either fat, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It happens, when you come to the treatment of the swelling, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument that is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring about our abscesses is that you take the most moist part of the body that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, as long as you feel that the instruments have perforated the heart, then it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the intermuscular, and beware in that which will be the result.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, which colour it has, thus make the dressing as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and after the intermuscular no moisture comes, know that it is fat, thus make a cross-shaped incision, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape each part and guard the cartilage where it seems you should pull it out with the knot;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if it stays still, it comes back to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it stays a little while, and the blood does not gush out, then apply to the wound some corrosive powders, and hold the wound, and put on soothing hot applications for abscesses, and treat with other treatments until it is healthy;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then sew the two lips of the wound, and treat with those things which induce scar formation.
