et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the veins are beaten against or otherwise hastened and apply to it a mixture of vitriol, and let it stay two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and restore the ebullition of blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to copper that which had been deposited from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Behold here the forms of the entromissive instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	Big and soft and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three kinds that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they have three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	big, soft, and small, for enclosing the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are like the needles whose sources are cut, and are of copper citrin, or iron, or silver, and some are worth more which are yellow, and are more tested with black lead for enclosing the cores of fistulas;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	big, soft, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the tumors are of many similarities, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	big, soft, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are wounds that have two cervices of three manners thus;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are wounds that have three cervices, and are thus of three manners;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are wounds that have two cervices, and wounds with only one cervice, and are of three manners;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary in their body.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is made thus sharp, and of such that they do not cut more than from one side, from which one scrapes the nuts, because one does not cut the vein nor the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these instruments are the scissors used in surgery, so that the patient does not feel at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use more force than on the flesh of the nuts, such as thighs, and arms, and shoulders, and the like parts.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to the fistula's scraper, in this form, to which one stains blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes at the place that bleeds with abundance of veins, and arteries, and sometimes breaks according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the shoulders of certain men become swollen when their humors begin to be corrupted, so that they seem to be the shoulders of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and they become swollen and inflated, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line from .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with warm medicinal tar, then bring together the two lips of the wound to suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs low, and is swollen due to its size as it happens in women, then make two incisions above, through two similar fissures;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	because one should hold the other at the end of one and the other, so that the longest line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line to the line.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said concerning stitching and powders, and that which is necessary in the treatment, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healthy, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the lack of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be until it reaches the marrow and the fat, then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that appear under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula, or it has knots, and if there is one that contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those which contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line B to line G:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole boil that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and let it be until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with gentle ointment suitable for that which is healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then do it as we have said in the incisions of scrofula, and if the wound is open, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin that is above it becomes swollen, often an abscess forms, and similarly it happens to the swollen vein with an abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus that it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the strangeness;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is due to the vein, then the feelings are of a feverish appearance;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to try to cure this abscess, and similarly when it is under the shoulders and arms and neck and in many other places, and it is very serious.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary then to avoid the treatment with iron, and the one who is in charge must avoid it also, and for the one who has a swollen artery, a lancet is made through the skin from far away;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the injury at the ankles, and carefully separate the artery from the tendons, until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then push a needle through one of the veins, and make it pierce to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread on both sides, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then touch the limb that is between the two threads of an intermedium as long as the blood which comes out of it, and let the abscess be opened;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then put in place the treatment that the wound requires, until the thread is pulled;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat what needs treatment, accordingly, until it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is near the size of the vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can from the abscess with all the skin, then push the needle through the limb that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	After the abscess, as I have told you, or the ligament of one of the two parts at the two sides of the flesh;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then you rethread another needle to all the thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess as long as the superfluous tissue comes out, then cut the superfluous part of the heart and let remain what is tied;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist cloth with wine and oil, then apply treatments of bandages and ointments until he is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses come to the artery and to the vein, abscesses come to the kidneys when they are injured, or from too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the joints and in the fingers and in all the limbs where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and in many cases it is without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one extracts it forcibly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in depth of the body, but rather near the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it moves well in all directions, and does not go neither forward nor backward, neither up nor down, and that which is in the joints does not require to be cut with iron;
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance it produces contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and that which is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin spitulous.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then suck it with the hook, and scratch it, then remove the bone and bring together the wound to the seam, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Hanging large boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it occurs in the belly and not in any other part of the body, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and large lumps.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and it has small and very large portions;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen a man who had two in his belly that were more similar to mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were easily split, and they corrupted the moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one eighteen ounces in weight, and in the other six, and the work of the incision is that you should examine if the patient's humors are moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and has a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If the scab is large on the spatula, and it is in your presence, then there is a cauterization by fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in the cutting often come very great outflows of blood, and if the wound is not treated, then hasten to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision of the iron, take a well-made thread of flax, and tie the joint as we have said, and let it be two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the thread of flax as long as it covers the joint, and cuts through it without effort;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, fear to cover them entirely for the belly, but you can cover half well, then cauterize so it does not grow back;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and beware that you do not cover the tissue which is of foul color and of poor sensation and of bad repair.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For there are hidden abscesses, and I will come to the treatment of abscesses after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the navel is swollen
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the navel comes from a cauterized wound or a crack in the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the navels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is visible, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of the skin and from the discharge of the navel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open to various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the discharge of the intestine, then it is even more diverse, and when one presses on the sides if they swell, and then subside, and by chance if they are obstructed, and increase greatly at the entrance of the bath and from strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it's a light thing, and it appears well when you press it with your hand, not constraining anything.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, it appears by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you consider its appearance by the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you abandon the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the belly, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his breath, and be stretched out straight, then sign with ink all around the navel.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then instruct them to sit comfortably between your hands, then go inside the bed that you have assigned to the whole spine, then place the majority of the abscess on top of the whole large uncle.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie him inside with a strong thread, or a cord of strong twisted rope firmly, and let us have the tied member loosened.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open the majority of the abscess stretched on the member, and thrust your right index finger, and seek the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it taken by the member, then untie it, and thrust the intestine to the bottom of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the navel, then take it by the hip, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein is made contrary, then go gently inside, then return to your work and take two needles, and thrust two forceps, and put the two needles inside what you have made in a cross that you make perforate.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four places under the ankles, and if you see, remove the ankles, and let the limb alone as long as it purifies, and discharge the dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or remove it when it becomes subtle and purified, then treat what is necessary, and discharge the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and strain the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the limb with what is necessary, and sew the limb.
dou chancre	of cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the section about the similarities of cancer, and how one should open with medicines, and how one should choose the treatment with iron;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that cancer grows in the marrow, and there is great difficulty in the treatment, and the ancients said that when there are cancers on the limb or where one can raise them like cancer which is in the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar limbs, and it must all be removed when it is in the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it does not matter that you approach it, for I have never seen any harm from it;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no harm has ever been seen by me before;
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the work, when it is in the body or where one can hide it, as we have said, is that you should sometimes purge the patient of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him do bloodletting if he has shown fullness, then prepare the patient well in body to perform the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then cut your nails or calluses, and shave yourself completely, and remove all the bone on every side without leaving anything;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and press well the body with your hand or with anything, and if the flow of blood makes you feel pain from the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it as long as the blood is stanched;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of another cure until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already spoken in the division about the symptoms of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each symptom, and the treatment that is made by medicines, and that which is treated with iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is broken with a sudden movement;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch with iron in these two symptoms:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	namely, tympanites and hypochondria, for it is mortal things;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you apply medicine to this symptom of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the treatment does not benefit, if consider that the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as a tumor and a solution of the stomach and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If he does not touch with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient with strong virtues, and he has no other illness except dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Lift the patient straight in your hands, and let the attendants press the belly with the elbow at the lowest part of the chest, then take the spatula spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	to a point, and the tube should not be so inserted that it can come into the intestine when one puts it in, and it cannot be blocked;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then consider if the dropsy is turned towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if necessary, you should cut into the arm three fingers from the elbow above the fist;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the hydropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then let the incision be on the left side of the belly III fingers;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it's due to the spleen, then let it be on the right, and it is necessary that the patient urinate on the incision so the superfluous liquids do not flow into the weak body;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce the skin with the instrument, and thrust it, and raise your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the underlying tissue as if scraping out the quantity of a fingernail or a small tumor;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the underlying tissue until the spatula comes to the empty space, and it is the seat of the pain, then pull it strongly, and thrust this instrument according to its shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver thread, and is made of light copper or brass, and has at its end a small perforation;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, a wound of three perforations;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two of another kind, and one of another;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that the writers carve into the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the upper part is the handle, so that when the strikers come to the water, they now descend onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	remove then the half or the third part, for if you remove more than it is necessary at that time, by chance the patient may die from the release of his vital spirit in the arm, or he may become paralyzed, or he may approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but remove according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then bring the instrument and hold the needle, and it is held now by the cord that stops up the perforation which is on the surface, of which I have spoken, that you should pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then insert the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take from the needle a small quantity;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do it on the same day, and keep yourself from touching him too much as long as there remains only a little bit of blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the patient, and you let much blood, so that the sore becomes swollen or rough, and by excessive sweating or bath and in the sun, and it turns black;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and treat with desiccative medicines until it be healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of blood, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes infants are born who do not have a hole in the rod, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it happens that he does not have to pierce all the very subtle spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put the subtle tube of a feather into the hole, and tie it with thread, and hold it for three or four hours, and when he wants to urinate, let the tube be removed, and let him urinate, and then put it back;
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance there is no harm, for the urine that comes forth does not allow it to be closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For he whose hole is small, there is a medicine of the thread of a feather, as we have said, which will enlarge it.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the hole in their place are called blind, for there are none born who have the hole at the head of the rod, because they cannot urinate before they lift their rod up high;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot put a splint on it because the material cannot come close to the marrow, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is that the patients lie on their back, put the head of the rod and the handle as the width of a quill, if the perforation is in the middle, as it is necessary;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the effusion of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, then stop the flow of what flows blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	the pustules of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times cysts come to the rod, and it is an appearance of flesh wound.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if necessary, you should take them with the sharp onion, and cut and clean all, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the joint with diafinicon as long as it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and putrid, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and the ulcer is on the edge, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the ulcer that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is swollen, then cure the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure it together, it is not assured that the edge of the ulcer will not be perforated, and comes blackness and corruption in its edge and in the gut.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply on it a plaster made of honey and flour which is made from the bark of pomegranate trees and lichen, then cure with other cures until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes from it, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cauteries are helpful in two conditions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	it is for knowing, for the flow of blood, and for the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the rod is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary that you put or conduct onto the rod a chain of lead, and let the patient urinate through it;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is tight around the head of the rod which is for those who have not been circumcised, or it is because of a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scratch with a sharpened instrument, so much that the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the rod is freed from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a grievous thing to divide this, then it is necessary that you scratch with a spatula or some pointed tool at the head of the rod and of the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then he must separate gently between II, and put I subtle bandage of wet linen on the cold limb, so that it does not stiffen again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	In every way when we do this work of our will, and especially for children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired by experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision in the hand, and with force, and all novelty;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if it happens to the heart that it has two tiles, and by chance if one covers this below and remains uncovered above.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	When the knee is injured, and the pain is doubled, and in the treatment that is given to it, the point of the member is not assured.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and in the treatment of the ankle by accident the iron escapes, and the work is ruined, and often it happens that they do not need treatment and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the treatment that is done to the threads of the string I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well both the healthy and the diseased.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in the whole stretch;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the threads are well enclosed within the leather;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not make him tie the thread to the rod so tightly, and then you make it come out in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then make it straight between your hands, and push the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the veins are not visible, nor any of the tendons.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then put your hand to the rod and blow into the wound, and pull it up high as long as the head of the rod is inside;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then clean it well of the pus that has accumulated, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it under the navel to the other navigation;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and tie it with the second ligature to the pouch and to the right index finger, and cut between the two threads, then lift the heart upwards hastily and pull the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	Then let the blood flow little by little, for it is a remedy;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on it and on the wound a plaster made from a mixture of cooked egg white, rose water, and oil, and let it be until the next day, and treat with another treatment as long as he is sick.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces at the mundification is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two parts should be held and should be cut, and the parts should be as large as the same size of the hands:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The mistake in the mundification is when the inner heart goes to the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then it is necessary that you stretch it with your finger, so that the limbs make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and shape it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, hold it with clamps, and then shape it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if it lasts three days, and that which is below the rod is swollen, then let it be until the abscesses are appeased, and the scab lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you shape it as you can, and guard the part of the rod, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Heal then the wound of things burned by powder, which we have said to treat with powders, and if one cuts beyond measure, and it goes to the sides, so it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal the wounds, as we have said, until they are healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of the urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from blockage of the kidney, or from frozen blood, or from bowel, or from dead flesh, or from similar things, which we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not discharged, and you see that the retention is due to the kidney which is stopped or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let his feet be placed on the back, and stretch his belly from the back to the upper part of the back, and constrain the patient's arm as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constricted by the pressure on the stone above, because of which the urine is dislocated;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of subtle silver, lightweight and hollow, like a bird's feather;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let its tube be a palm and a half in length, and let it be subtle at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of issuing the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at the end a small piece of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess of the wool and push it just to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and with egg white, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and the rod with moist oil of olive and of tallow;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then lightly put the syringe on the rod, until it reaches the root of the rod, then fold the rod back towards the bundle.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming up to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless for that which leads where it goes is twisted;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then insert the thread into all of the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and reintroduce the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scales or blood come into the bladder, or when putridness is assembled, and you see distillations of sharp remedies, then make all the instrument that is called "clyster", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two of one kind, and one of another, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the limbs are shaved because the medicine should be such that it cuts well the stick without addition, if one can then treat the moisture, and beat when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see that your medications are in the bladder, put the head of the caster in the moisture, and treat the one who is inside;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you treat the moisture with the caster, and then strongly beat the one who is inside;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moistures enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle syringe with which one injects into the bladder:
si est ci:	it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of brass, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and remove to the fat the bad blood;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you want to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a twisted thread of wool, and heat that moisture on the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the end of the cleanser in the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder to extract all the moisture completely, until the patient feels that the moisture has gone into the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle with it, and pierce it all around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread through these holes, then join the circle as one joins a bag, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do so as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already spoken in the division of the ways of stones, and the extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and have said the difference between the stone in the kidneys as testicles, and all the symptoms, and in which stone one should operate with a cut;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the rod;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder often happens to children, and it's a sign that the water of the bladder is similar to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it openly injures, and troubles the patient's rod, and causes them to urinate many times, and then strangles;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and in many of these wounds the foundations
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and the healing of children is easy until they are 4 years old, and is very grievous in old men, and is similar to the young, for those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the treatment is easier for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with enemas, in order to purge all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and bend and move to the bottom, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from the high place;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands are below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declined downwards;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then touch the wound from inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the bladder, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall upon touching everything, anoint your right index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is old, or your right middle finger, if the patient is a young adult;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and thrust it to its foundation, and touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, if it sticks to the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on with your finger, and thrust it downwards where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand hold the skin which is below the intestines in the area where the incision is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then he wraps the spatula with a bandage, from which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make between that which is between the intestines and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left navel;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and let it be straight on the stone, and the two edges be even or equal to the fundament, and let the width of the strip be such that it is wide by width, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance the press if the edge which is on the fundament, so that it jumps without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is a part of stone where it has corners and edges:
si est griés a issir;	thus it is easy to extract;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if the part that is swallowed, resembles a nut, and is round, of which the exit is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	At the sky hence where it has corners and edges, make the cut larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not heal, then you must extract on the tendons that are as tight as a line to the head, for over-tightening the stone so that it does not shatter;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you apply beneath the subtle curved instrument to the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot introduce it thus, then enlarge a little the perforation, and without unraveling, extract with a glass tube;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if it has more than one stone, then put first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut into it, then pull downward, and the small ones afterward if there are several;
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it is necessary to operate, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For these things have happened to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	where it dies, or the urine comes out again through the place where the limbs cannot solder;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless you force to pull, or to strip the tendons, until you pull it apart by pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, then apply the plaster of incense and of balm and of dragon's blood, and strain it, and put on top a moistened cloth in oil and in wine, or in oil and in hot rose and cold rose, to appease the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then sit the patient up on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, then anoint the limb well with oil and rosewater, then treat it with ointment of galbanum and ointment of basil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if an abscess forms in the wound and ulcers, and there is a coagulation of blood in the bladder, and the urine is retained by this means, which is connected in such a way that without exit with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then put your finger into the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and rot it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then elevate the wound from the cold and the draft and the humidity, and aid it in all the ways that you know, until it is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the parts that you cure, that you tie the two thighs, and apply the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the penis, and stuck in, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the treatment of what I say is not effective, that you often cut, it is excused from the cutting for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron instrument in this shape and let it be with three angled points in one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take the thread and tie it around the rod under the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the instrument into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the instrument with your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if urine comes out at that time, then press your hand on the part which remains of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is thus broken, and the blood comes out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do it for any thing that is lacking, then tie the thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod straight on the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal them as long as they are healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the bladder of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that the bladder is injured in women, and if it does happen, then the treatment is grievous, and is forbidden for three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that by chance the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-versed and aware of her own body, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in this art with her hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is that the bladder of the woman is deeper than that of the man, because it requires making a deeper incision, and there is great danger. And if it is necessary to do so, then it is required that you take a wise midwife, and with points investigate thoroughly, and if you do not find it, ask for the wisest and most subtle midwife;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present to them a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and instruct her to do what you instruct regarding the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and observe very well if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to put her hand or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, if the pain presses her hand, and instruct her to put her hand or with the patient, and seek and press her left hand on the belly firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gently from the entrance of the belly down, as far as it comes to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the womb, where it appears to be misplaced, and feel the stone in that area;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and let his finger move under the stone or above, and let the cut be small at first;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then probe the wound with a small instrument, if you feel the stone growing in the plaque so much that the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to recognize the disease.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the blood does not stop, then put on the wound a warm application of vitriol, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stanched;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone for men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the blood does not come out, and it is from the artery that is cut, then put powder on the wound and constrain with tourniquets and bandages, and do not restart this, and leave the stone alone and do not extract it, lest by chance the patient would die;
puis cure la plaie.	then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limbs are strengthened, then return to your work, as long as the stone is not removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Rumor aqueous is nothing but an accumulation of moisture or whitish fluid, which is discharged from the heart of the kidneys, that contains the urine;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly found in the fabric of the urine, so that one thinks this is another urine;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it's the skin of the ankle between the white skin that we have spoken of;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this does not happen to few people.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is from weakness that comes to the ankles, and the material spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the ankles, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it's a color declining to yellow, or it's without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of recognizing this gathering, for if it is or white skin that we have spoken of, then there are abscesses behind, a little long as the figure of an egg, and the ankles do not appear, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own layer, then there are abscesses behind with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it's another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the legs and the white surface, then it seems good to him;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you want to know the color of the moisture, investigate thoroughly in all the intermuscular spaces, because of which the shape is formed in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intermuscular, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the replenishment of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then put a cushion under his back, on something a little high, and put many towels under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left, and instruct the servant to sit on the right, and stretch the rod to one of the two ribs at the side of the legs;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula in hand, and cut the skin of the legs in length as far as the knee, and let the incision be straight, dividing the skin of the legs to the white surface, and scrape subtly according to his power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the syphac with a needle of the vein to the large perforation, and extract the entire vein, and then put your clamps, and let the syphac be above;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the heart of the intestines, but only the syphac;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut all or in pieces, removing the subtle costa from it, that if you do not cut well wisely, the vein will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the ulcer heals quickly on its own, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the vein;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then assemble the two lips of the intestine's opening to a suture, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to ligate the vessels that are suspended, doubting the decrement of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut around the navel, and extract the vein, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the team is assembled into two parties together, know that these are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	Cut the other part just as you did the first equally, then suck out the blood, and put on the wound a moist linen cloth in oil or rose water;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on another moist linen cloth in wine and oil, and put on the two navels, and put above them doubled blankets, and tie it all up with a string which is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with linen dressing according to this likeness and let them be assembled by sewing on the throat of the arms, and one of the hands hold it at the bottom against the back, and the other at the part of the groin;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two veins at the ankles, and let the whole assembly of the restraint be in the bend of the arm;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this kind of cauterization is applied to the iron cautery on the body, and it is that you take a fine surgical cautery, and cut the skin of the intestines, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white skin that contains the ailment is discovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery in this manner, and pierce that skin with the sharp edge, and scrape it with this fine hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut in all the ways that you can, until you have scraped everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and beware that the fat does not touch the bone;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more beneficial to health;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of the flowing of blood, and doctors who are unskilled in surgery;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you contrary, or an abscess forms or a flow of blood or another thing, then cure that which makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this treatment due to its horror, then perform perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that the humor is at the site, then make the patient sit on a elevated seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the part below at all the spatula to the width, and put the perforation along the length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the opening be wide, so that the whole water can flow out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the remaining water flow out, then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white fabric does not allow the pus to exit from the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you apply a bandage or the instrument with which one treats the pus of dropsical patients, whose shape is thus described;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the pus returns, and it is assembled after six months or in which interval, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the intestines
