Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this branch there is fear in many conditions, because it seems to me that moving it is better than leaving it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and especially to the intestines;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to be known by a surplus of bitter and sharp humour, which is spread to the intestines, or from a blow;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and it is the colour of the abscess according to the colour of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not find a point of pain, and is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance is an abscess which is grievous, foul and stone-like, and of a dark colour, and sometimes comes from a corruption of artery, or from an inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a corruption of an artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press on it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not suitable that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from an inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition to the expression of touching with the fingers, and can make a good diagnosis based on this similarity, and on other symptoms;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut around the area of the abscesses, then the pus comes out, and the white skin above it, and delivers the suspensor from all parts of the abscess.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the pus is already swollen with these new wounds, then it is necessary that you draw out the pus, and cut around it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is near the skin, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver the entire tendon, and cut around it completely.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the growth of the wound is in the back of the limb, then it is necessary that you cut it entirely, and extract the pus, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the work is accomplished, then apply the wound with a moist plaster of oil and wine, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the boils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	These are abscesses enveloped in an envelope resembling a bud, with the softening of the boils, and the patient complains grievously when he walks;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this illness is just as frightening as the one before, and nevertheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a seat that alleviates it, then apply the suspensor to the boils below your fingers, to all the vessels that are near the privy parts, and tie the masters, and extend them forcibly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with the spatula, cutting widely through to open up the vessels, as long as they are discovered, and then scrape from each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then he fixes a needle where it has a double thread, and ties it to the first wound where the blood came, and ties it on the other side;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then he cuts them in the middle straightforwardly, according to the length of the body, and removes the corrupted humors;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then he cures the wound like the others or applies a poultice, so that no vessel bursts which would nourish one of the ulcers;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For from this comes no evil, and if all the vessels come to life, then it is necessary to treat the ulcers with regard to all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the bones do not lose their nourishment due to the cutting of the vessels, and dry and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The coming of this illness is from the section that comes to the spleen, or the stretching on the belly in the area of the ribs, because the intestine descends from that rupture to one of the ulcers;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this curvature is from the pain of the liver, or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	from a blow, or from a jump, or from a blow with the arm, or from lifting of heavy objects, and from similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the symptoms when it is from the extension of the liver, are that they come on little by little, in a long stretch, and do not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are even up to the depth, because the liver presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the symptoms are when it is from the affection of the liver, that it causes sudden pain to appear, and there are diverse abscesses appearing under the skin, pressed close, and it is due to the escape of the intestine and the body being weakened by the liver.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines adhere to the liver, and are retained there, and cause great pain for the patient to suffer, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with fear, because of which he must avoid.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to put his hand inside the wound to repair the intestine if it can be returned.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let him sit on your neck, between your hands, and lift up the thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the intestines from along the length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put within the liver of the waist, twelve inches according to what you have as a task for opening the wound, and let it be such that the bones can come out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape the thin layer that is beneath the skin of the intestines, until the white thin layer is exposed on all parts;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your right index finger in that which enters the intestine, in that which is between the white thin layer that is beneath the skin of the navel, and between the second thin layer, and separate that which is behind the navel, and between the second thin layer;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move to the right hand within the heart of the intestines, and let the white surface appear on top at your left hand, and raise the upper part towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to stretch the upper part upwards, and untie that which is tied behind the bandage;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your fingers if there is a point on the intestine that has an enveloped or white hard surface, and if you find anything, then push it down to the bottom of the belly;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle or one with a large thread made of threads, and push it into the rear part of the surface, which is behind the skin of the intestines;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the heads that appear with threads, until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the surface, which we have spoken of, that is behind the skin of the intestines, with a strong thread of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then envelop the heads of the veins, and tie them in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter into them, lest the abscess should grow.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put a ligature according to the first ligature long two fingers of that one, and after these two ligatures leave two threads which are hidden near the heart of the body the size of a finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the swelling brings;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is near the skin of the body, as far as the blood and the flesh, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then put a moist bandage in oil, and apply it to the wound, and also apply the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the aforementioned swelling is cauterized, after the incision, due to suspicion of a decrease in blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens often, and leaves the ligament as long as it dries by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it is late in healing, apply a warm poultice, and put on what we have said, until it dries;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this weakness I have never seen anyone who dare to make the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is made like the weakness which is assembled to the bowels, in such a way that you bind the vessels, after the cut above and below lightly with dressings;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of what has happened, until the vessels dry;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes swelling comes to the shoulders, as we have said, and it opens the joints;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and does not touch any of the intestines to the bowels, and if they do touch them, it is little, and repairs all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and however if it stays too long in this spot, the wound or catarh grows, until the intestine touches;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens due to the extension of the cataract which is in the shoulders, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swollen are the joints and opened;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the cure is by cauterization, as we have previously said;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient puts his back between your hands, then cut the joint of the swollen shoulder according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the skin flap that is underneath the skin which is called the membrane, then take the fat and put it on the apparent bone of the flap;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press to the bottom of the belly, then sew the two apparent bones of the flap on the head of the fat, and sew one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the fat, and do not cover any point of the flap nor extend the vein to anything else, as I have made you know in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then heal it by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you sew the skin, if it becomes infected and treat the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The flap is constricted, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cauterizations are moved on this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times is softened the skin of the intestines in some men, because the entrails that are inside are made soft, and it is bad to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on his back, and to cut the softened skin on the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two lips together to a stitch, and if you see, first cut away the excess of softened skin to three stitches or four firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the stitches, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and tighten the thread.
dou chastrement	of the treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Purging is included in our law, and for this reason it pleases me that I do not speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary to use force for the two manners:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the doctor responds with wisdom when one asks him, and with wisdom the treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have need of the chastisement of certain beasts to help us, such as goats and rams and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say then that punishment is done according to two methods:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by traction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we do by traction, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the joint is softened and flexible;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then we take them with our hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the punishment of cutting:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then lift it up, and cut above each hoof, as soon as you have well examined them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and let none of the thick skin and the subtle skin which is on the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of punishment is better than that which is made by traction, because in traction something from the intestines often remains by chance, for which the beast desires luxury;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then treat the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphrodite is in two manners to men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two hips appears as if the figure of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes outside there is urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the genitals as if a penis and two hips.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the man and the woman is that you cut the adjacent flesh all around, and treat it as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the kidneys, there is no point of cure.
de la tentigene	of the tendons or sinews
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	The tendon is a cord joined to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary to hold the excess of the tendon with your hand or with the nails, and cut it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deep in the flesh, lest a flow of blood come, for one cure drives out another cure as long as it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and for another sore that is born at the mouth of the marrow, and the filling, and by chance breaks out, and is similar in appearance to a cow's, and for this they call it the ancient "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to amputate, as we have said the incision, and the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of rheumatic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Rheumatism is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to be;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is from heat adjusted, or from subtle or sharp humor, and it is made in the marrow, or in the sides, or in the back, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevents conception, and childbirth, and by chance causes flowers to have;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is through the observation of the urine.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears to be near the fingers or the veins.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle and sharp humor, and it is near the kidneys, then hasten, and bend the knee:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	Then stretch the two labia majora, as much as the subtle vulva skin is rounded, and let the stoppages be covered;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take the needle, and anoint it with oil, and put it on the place, and give the woman a house remedy each day, so that she cannot suffer.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the vulva is hard and swollen, then it is necessary to cut the spatium resembling a knife to the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the stoppages are made of new flesh, then suck on the onion and cut it;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and apply the blood-stanching medications, such as haemostatic, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with some oil;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	Then put on a bandage of wide cloth, so that the wound cannot suffer;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it be for a long time, and apply a bandage of dry flax.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let him be cured with other cures until he is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes new flesh, if it is necessary to cover it in this manner, then it is not an abscess that forms.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that forms in the marrow, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are ruptures of veins to which a custom arises, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become weak.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the weakness, when they are deep in the marrow and do not appear to feeling, are not cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the stomach, one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, afterwards apply warm bandages, and bind it at its roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then put her feet in warm water for an hour, then put her in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if discharge of blood comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumach and the bark of pomegranate trees and of gall and similar things, and then take flour of barley, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster to put on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stains, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that is not so, then have cauterized the ventouses on the back and the same for the sides to strike;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take the wool, and the mallet in juice of plantain or in juice of aglentier with old wine, and cauterize on the spot.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess has burst, then treat the place of the wound as long as it is sore;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it is necessary to scrape as I have said in the previous theorem;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the marrow, such as cancer and apostema, pierous and herpes and eczemas and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have spoken of in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary then that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that affect the bowel.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, then observe that the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hurry to pierce, but make an incision as long as the pain is alleviated;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and let him have two small seats or where he can lean, and support himself on his back and gather his feet together as far apart from the thigh;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a linen band;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then suck the bulge towards the right side, and insert the instrument through which one evacuates the mouth of the abscess, from which afterwards comes the shape;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you have seen the instrument inserted, that you fix the rod first to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go more deeply than it should, and that it does not harm the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instruments are large, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not injure it;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he puts the horn of the instrument to the bottom, and that he holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses open, and one makes a soft hand, then it is necessary to cover the head with a spatula, to the left;
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is empty, it is necessary that you put in the wound moist tents in rose oil or in dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the tent far from the wound at the bottom of the marrow, and put on top of the marrow and on the bandage a clean moist cloth in water or wine if they are cooked;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat afterwards for two days with oil having arrived at that place, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and sometimes raise the marrow and the wound with a cluster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and dried aristolochia, if they are cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is pushed back into the marrow, it is necessary that you guard against iron cauterization, but rather treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of the swelling
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	The midwife is first to examine the natural shape of the swelling, and its signs when you see the woman approaching from below, and wants to smell the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then the fetus hurries to come out with force;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then you will know that this swelling is according to the natural shape, and it comes out from its head, and the second with it;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, then you should gently press her belly, so that the fetus comes out completely;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends from its head, then the second one comes with it, and the mother is freed from her superfluities by good purification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes abnormally does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes from its feet, and comes force against the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes from its belly, or penis, and is turned by chance over its neck, and by other deformed shapes;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the healer to be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the methods as one ought to help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the afterbirth comes out naturally, and the woman gives birth easily, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or let the women hold her.
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and let its natural oil or rendered fat be cooked, and then let the healer insert between her thighs the small spatula, of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and cut the second layer, and cut to one's nail as much as the mucus that is in the corpse of the fingers;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press on the woman's belly until the afterbirth comes down, and if it does not come down, then it is necessary to give the woman an enema of rendered fat with oil of cypress;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make them press and stretch the condyls, and hold their mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if it is now in the sinews.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands are swollen, then you must reset them lightly little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then remove the seat from the ground, and hold onto the woman, so she does not fall with the removal;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the sinews are dead, then cut the hands at the joint which is placed there before, and extract the infant, and reset evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the infant on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the sinews come to the feet, then it is necessary to push from above;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps just above the hips, if it is commanded to be grasped, and the leg is stretched by condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps far, God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go far as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take a muscle of the thigh, and oil of Kisam, and melted gum, and pound all in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and apply this ointment to the nature of the woman within and without, then make her sit in a warm bath until the hips are soaked;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is swollen, make for him a plaster of myrrh, and put it on, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make him sit on a seat, then make him throw up and hold his mouth and nose, and press his belly gently, for the swelling will go down now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the discharge of the infant upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the swelling comes in this manner, then put a poultice on his hands a little and a little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then let it be applied to his neck, and his feet hang down, and let him lie in the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and rub his hands a little and a little, and then press his hands on the belly, and remove the cushions from under him, until it is prepared below;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the swelling does not go down, then take his feet and move them strongly, then move the belly upwards, then beat your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and little by little the child vomits;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to hold herself so that the fetus is pressed.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who has one arm outside
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if you cannot bring it back, have the woman get up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed, and stretch out her legs forcibly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then anoint the muscle that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not deliver, have her sit on a seat, then make an effort to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and deliver the child according to its natural position, and have it turned, and instruct her to hold herself so that the fetus is pressed out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and it has expanded its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back;
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the patient holds his hand, then turns it little by little, and lifts the arm lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, put on the natural muscle of the upper arm and elbow, as we have said, then instruct that it moves little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make him sit on a seat, and instruct him to take himself;
et la fai esternuer.	and make him stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner for the whole second one
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this manner for the whole second one, cut the second one with your nail, until the mucus is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if it enters into his face and neck, then cut it from the mouth, so it is not retained, and remove the mucus;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then turn the infant from within, until you have put it as it is necessary, and instruct the woman to take herself at another time:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then it will easily straighten.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the exit of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	It is known that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if rarely named;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they should be multiplied, and are divided by the liver which conceives them, which is tied to the navel;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out naturally like all the other foetus, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out quickly, then the treatment is as we have said, and let the subtle bath, and make everything light and easy what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it is worth for health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Certain times they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or many up to XV, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious sage, and it is necessary that the wise woman knows all this, for by chance similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	thus do according to what is necessary
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of the dead or stillborn child, as I have said in the section, and it does not come out, and you are forced to perform a manual operation;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of good virtue, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her thighs be bent downwards, and her legs be raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife applies the bandage of two parts, or it is tied to the bed so that it is not treated for the descent of the infant;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the newborn with moistened oils of nutmeg and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint its hands with these oils and these rubbings;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently rock the newborn, then turn it on its side where it rocks the elbows that are suitable for that, and take care that the infant is prepared so that it descends onto its chest;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if it puts its elbows in its eyes or on its neck or in its mouth or on its palate or under the beard or in the armpit or near the ribs, and if the descending is onto its feet, then it will put or prick and has wounded sides;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he takes the onion with his right hand, and puts the curve between the two fingers of the left hand, and bends all his hand lightly, and inserts the onion into one of those places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert one against another onion, or thou thyself in this craft, so that the extraction be even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to another, for the sake of extraction, and let the onions be held by the teeth, as this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then anoint the ball with some of his fingers of oil, and put them in that part, and pull out the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains a point, then put this onion in a higher place, and do this until everything goes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to the strain, then you must wrap it in a bandage, as long as it is swollen;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then put the cup on the joint of the sole of the foot or on the heel, and thus you must do on the other hand, and on the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the infant is large and it is constricted in the birth passage, or it has an assembled or tangled head, then you must put the spinous spondulus between your fingers, and make the head and extract the shoulder;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you round it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus same make the veins have a large natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then draw the bones to the tendons, and if the head is sound and it holds by strength, even if it is cracked, as long as the moisture that is in the bottom comes out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces with the knife that you hold;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce through until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, then the treatment is gentle, and the adjustment to the mouth of the marrow is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is narrow in the belly or in the chest, then it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and pierce the belly or the chest, until the moisture that is there flows;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are swollen, and the head remains still, then take the balance of his hand in front of the marrow, and draw it just to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then anoint the wound with one or two ounces of oil, and apply the bandage;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the abscess is constricted by hot aposteme that has come to it, then it is not necessary to operate, but rather to apply warm and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and let the plasters be applied, and put in water softening and moistening substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, then apply what we have said for a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and let no one touch it, so apply the bandage in pieces, and do not leave anything of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, apply what we have said regarding hot abscesses that come to the abscess;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a flow of blood comes, then it should be put in astringent water, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had a dead infant, then one congealed on that, and the other was also dead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long tension, he came to have abscesses on his navel, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to suppurate greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not cauterize the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no pointed bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead infant.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I searched the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman urinated for a long time afterwards, and also issued a little bit of bile from the body;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not recalled this chapter before because of that, when the masters find a strange thing, they know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the hammer back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Then comes the shape of the presser, where one turns the limbs;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to the two turnings at the two heads of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	In all ways, the horns should be more subtle than the restrainer, and made from ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the wooden one two fingers in width, and the margin of the trees two fingers, and a palm and a half in length;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are fixed on one and on the other, half a palm in length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are placed in the mouth of the hammer to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, made similar to it but more subtle and lighter, should be made of the wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the similarity of the tendons.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two heads two joints, as you see, one palm in length, and two fingers in width;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see to open the marrow to all the instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, the feet hanging and the legs spread, then put the two joints joined together in the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument separated between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then put your hand on the instrument, as you have done with the tendons equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the marrow, until the ball makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all mounted, and are multiplied in their similarities;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the eyes are prepared, so much more swift is the work, and higher are the men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you do not have prepared, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in the infant, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her expel the mucus, and hold her hands at the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she spits through that, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take the vessel, and make a poultice or suppository, and put in it herbs that can open the mouth of the matrix, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or put in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	Then put a cane or stick through the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marrow, and hold it until the vapors come out from inside the marrow;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then do the rubbing, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is injured.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not better, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in mastiche of nutmeg, and then put it on the affected area, and treat the second joint;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, if she takes it and slowly stretches it straight, so that the marrow does not break with the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but then you should gently move it to the right and to the left, and then pull;
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and disentangles.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the thigh is constricted, we have said the treatment of purification, and of fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from all that which we have said, beware that you do not foolishly touch the tendon;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that which is at the mouth of the thigh, that you bind it to the hip of the woman, then anoint her with Tetrapharmacum ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if the poultice is applied and replaced, and comes a fever;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but in any case, when it suppurates if there comes bad smell to the stomach and to the head, and troubles the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	If then there is need for fumigations of cubebales for that:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	some of the ancients have experienced fumigation with croton and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one purges the woman with retention of the flowers and of the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to be seen similar to a chain, and put the thin head into the nature, and the wide feet on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the cauterization as long as it is wasted, and start again with another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, instead the passage is stopped up with a thin mucus:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	then it is necessary to the nurse that she pierce that mucus with her finger, and not pierce the tender spatule, and warn the child that it not touch;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the moistened spot with wine and oil, then the treatment of anointing as long as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not straighten, then put or pass a chain of wool, and let the hands be still, and be careful when the veins want to go into the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes there comes sudden swelling of a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to treat that one suddenly:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	it should be treated, as we have said regarding the chain of wool.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from the bottom are an annoyance, and worse than those that come from the bottom of the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, either to one fistula or more;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that annoyance is old, it works, and increases moisture with white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by that which comes out in evacuation or flatulence when the patient has diarrhea, and by chance in jumping of a vessel.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that reach just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the rod;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they come close to the joint of the thigh, and close to the hollow of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the fistula that penetrates to the foundation, and does not penetrate:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your finger to the index or foundation, and apply a subtle needle of spider or iron in the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then apply a thread of delicate flax, or the hair of a horse, until you feel the thread or the hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come through evacuation or flatulence or urine, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	let them know that they do not penetrate deeply;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to apply a cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is near the bladder or near the passage of the urine, if it cuts off the flow of urine, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced near the joint of the thigh, then the tendon comes near the flesh;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the invention of the pain inside, then it is that it comes from the elbow, and not worth a medicine or a dressing with oil;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistulas near the skin there is no cure except for work, and vanity of foolish doctors who insert themselves.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one that is not near the skin and is not ancient, there is hope of health through cauterization, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient puts between your hands on their back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined to his stomach;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then he pulls out a piece of arrow, or of lance if there is a fracture, until you know where the piece comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it inside the foundation, then you must pull out your second finger, if afterwards it seems that the piece has perforated;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and is discovered where you feel between your fingers the spleen or the flesh, then know that it is pierced;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if not working on it one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can heal some with all methods, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that one gives, is to apply the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and thrust all hot into the fistula, until it reaches the bottom;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these false ulcers are cauterized, which resemble a peacock's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with wet tents in butter, until that false ulcer is raw, then treat with a greasy ointment and searing and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	For that, nothing else can be healing;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if it has a tent between, and does not perforate just to the finger that is at the bottom, and between your finger and the tent a thick cover of flesh or of scab, and you see the fistula in this which follows the cover of the abscess;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and thrust immediately before the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tendon will be delivered, and will fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then I define those fallen charms that seem a pin of bone, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood comes to an end, and cuts between you and the work, then the cauterization of fire or of sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the cauterizations of fire join two bone things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	it is to know, the articulation of these joined charms, and the stopping of blood and the drying of the moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of moist tendons in butter or in crushed things, until the limbs give ease, and thus the charms are set in the ease;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound of sudden injuries with hard charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from deep within the foundation, and it is separated from the body, then apply a poultice to the bottom or foundation, and inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between two is the web or the skin or flesh, or it is pressed to pierce, if there is not a way of escape and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut from the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tendons that hold the foundation, and come to the egutions by the willful sensibilities;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by adventure it will be healthy, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut deep within the foundation, either by tent or by another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then anoint the wound with that ointment which is in the plaster, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part opposed to the foundation:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And often are fistulas in this manner:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you push the thread into the fistula, and it is or touches the bottom of the foundation beneath the skin, if take a thread pierced at the head in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I push the twisted thread into II, and push the thread with all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it passes in the margin of the bottom within, then pull out the thread from that which has passed through, so that you push your finger on the bottom;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and draw the head of the thread, and assemble the two parts together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and hold it in place several times, until the thread joins these parts that are between the two, and adheres;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all ways that you can, if the flesh is not too thick.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make a incision through the thick flesh, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the sharp spinous spatula that one makes for the fistula is very pointed at one end and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, because one does not join what one should not join, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the swollen areas
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Swollen areas are according to two methods:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and sometimes with blood, and there is one or several, and they are on the surface of the foundation and at the head of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are on the surface have little moisture, and sometimes have a little yellowish or greenish discharge, or a little blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them within the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to squeeze himself in chambers, until the foundations issue forth, and the fibers appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry it, and hold it with forceps, or you hold it on your nail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the ulcers cannot be held back by their moisture, then they take to the scalpel, or to the cauterizing iron, or to a piece of chamel.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them with the tongs, then cut them, and powder above some warm powders that are in the cauterizing iron;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then cure them with other cures until they are healthy;
