et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot be evacuated, then give the patient a sharp and bitter enema to wash out what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the sick person feels better, and if the thread is pulled from the bottom, then the treatment is a light one;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them with your nail or with the pincers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear not the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it happens that you must perform the cauterization in this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a thread, and put it on a needle, and then draw the thread through and make the needle penetrate from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread around the needle, and let it be of the width;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus to all the others, and leave one to stop the excessive flow of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a moistened cloth dipped in rose oil or in cerate, and apply it to the foundation, and instruct the patient that he should rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it be until it adheres, and when they have adhered, apply the treatment of bandage and other treatments, until he is healthy;
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Dryness of the liver or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the liver in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no value.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you touch the point of a spatula or on one angle the outer skin, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it as long as it is swollen as it is necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be treated, then resume the rubbing stronger than before, until it bleeds much, and becomes scarred;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it as long as it is wounded.
dou fremit	of a tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Furnacle is a small false appearance in the body, and goes very deep inside;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the cold, and one feels it as if dead from trembling, and it comes into the whole body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a vein from a wing of a goose, or a wing of a strong cultural, and put that vein on the forehead, so that the circles completely enclose the forehead inside;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to take the vein all around so that you bind all around the forehead, and put it in the background, and clear the forehead of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make it from a vein of copper or iron in this form, and be subtle below and pull above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	nor prick, for it is enough to hold and press.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, cauterize the forehead, as it is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cystere
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes they make a cystere of silver or gold, or of melted copper or enamel;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes they make of these small and large instruments, according to what they are needed for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These things that one needs in the treatment of children and who are weak and ailing, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clamp, small and large, is thus wide, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and it has a separation where the belly should be tied, as you see, and the thing is perceived within;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and it has on one of its sides two openings, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly or bag is made with medicines of a beast's bladder or of parchment, and is perforated all around with small openings, and has between each opening one thread of space, then sewn in these openings one strong thread of twisted cord, and assemble the belly as it is a sack;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, then apply a ligature in front of a strong thread, then give a clyster.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or with a gentle ointment, or a similar thing, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the minister closes his two hands together as long as it takes, then withdraws the clyster, and lifts the patient's legs to his belly, and if the medicine wants to come out, holds it back as long as he can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a night in this way, it is more beneficial help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him for a disease of cleansing of the stomach, and the medicine hastens to come out, then retain it as long as he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if there are ulcers or abscesses at the foundation, or apostemes, then the cluster should be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the form of a subtle cluster on which the skin is tight:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places or where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are pieces of stone, and cuts of sword and of knife, or of lance or of stick or of arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that cuts on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory of them comes in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is large, and you suspect a warm abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it makes so much blood from the head injury that it comes forth a little blood from the wound, and let the blood be on the contrary side of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and forbid the patient excess of wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be diminished, and let him not drink wine, nor eat a lot of meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if abscesses or a tumor comes, cotton moistened in oil or rose water, or in wine to apply;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder, which I will discuss a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the blood has been stirred, then put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by stitches, then assemble them by sewing, as I will discuss for wounds of the belly, concerning the sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is uncovered to the bone, and hangs, and does not hold except for a little, then cover it;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then heal the wound with medicine, and restore the scar tissue in the skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, such as boiled and roasted meat, also like birds, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a rotten place on the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut out all the rotten part, and apply force, then heal it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has cut an artery in the wound or vein, without caution, and it cannot be stanched by medicine, then seek the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put in this powder which dries as soon as the blood has been shed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	Take incense in part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	blood of dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	carnelian alive three parts, and powder subtly, and apply to the wound, and extract firmly, until it adheres well and joins to all its flesh;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and let it be without unbinding, so it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this with carnelian alone, when one does not have incense or blood of dragon, but that the arsenic has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has moved the wound, likewise in summer, if one does not put on this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it is fully healed;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal other healings as long as he is healthy
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pinces.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, do not apply any other treatment than to leave it alone, and do not put anything constricting, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medicine be soothing, as warm water is applied to sweet oil, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked in warm water, and other stones of mining done in this manner, and ointments moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it with bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hollow and full of pus, then puncture or lower the abscess;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and with flowing blood comes, then dissect it, and ligate it, and cauterize, this is the surgeon's job;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the gullet of the throat is cut, or the trachea, and the conduit is blocked, through which the food goes, then sew the trachea to the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it back with bandages, and let some hours pass, then treat the dislocations of the joints for as long as it is wounded;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, thus the tumor;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, thus the fractured parts that you can put back, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound suppurates, and is evacuated and the discharge is loosened;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a spear or of a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a spear or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look at the wound to estimate how much blood the patient has lost:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	It seems then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it with the blood that has not stopped flowing, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I apply attractive ointment, and bind it to him twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, then put in the wound a lot of cotton to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if no spasm or trembling of the heart occurs, nor strangulation of the limbs;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the bones in their proper place, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the thenar of tents and other treatments, as long as it is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and becomes open, show that it has become fistulous;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is as one ought.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword cut or a knife, and it is simple, or in the foot or on the back, then treat what is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, of stitching;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and in a cut in several pieces, thus cauterize the wound, and the torn parts if they are separated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not separated, then let the wound rot, to ease the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Drop of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The drops from the rupture of the belly are great and frequent and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound often comes out the intestine, or the knots of the intestines, by which the intrusion of the guts;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more troublesome, and often worse than the small wound the large one, because one puts back in more carefully the intestines, if one does not put them back quickly while still hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestine swells as soon as it feels the cold, if they are put back in more carefully, and for this reason the middle wound is worse, because one puts back most of the intestine to its place than the others;
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common stitches have in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of the other wounds of the body and the other special stitches are common to the other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all of them are more prone to injury of the belly, and I will tell and declare each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and a thing from the intestine comes out, and it's difficult to put back, it is by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is weakened by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is frozen, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or a cloth in hot water only, or you heat it with boiling water and pepper and cypress, and apply it to the intestine until the frozen part is thawed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this treatment must be repeated, and it's necessary that you apply it to soothe and to unfreeze.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the inflation departing, anoint the intestine with water or oil and evil humors are cooked, for by this is alleviated the entrance to a little of thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, make a little wound at the instrument through which one collects the humors;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to move the stone, that we should not cut without great necessity or need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	then cut within the concavity and do not cut through, and see to it the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine is healthy and strong, then put it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power to do so, for this is a good thing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the upper part of the belly, then put the head and the chest higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts then put attention to that so the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say for large and weak wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds put what is suitable for you, then take it between your hands and administer gently so that it reaches all the rupture with its effect, and bring the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common manner of sutures, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound two fingers' space, and stick a needle where it has strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the suture, which is underneath the skin, until you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two ends of the suture in four gathered;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain the thread of a double cord around the needle of two parts, then assemble the two heads of the wound together, and then let the thread of the suture, and attach another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then thread the cord as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to your skill with the needles, until the entire wound is restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be moderate, between subtle and coarse, for the subtle needles take all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for it is fitting that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not fitting to push the needles too far into the flesh and through the skin, so that they do not catch and close the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then catch the heads of the needles, so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put tents or dressings on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and let them be until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this manner of treatment of the needles is more suitable for small wounds, for it suffices a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second treatment is common, and it is that you assemble the two parts of the skin and the two parts of the fascia together with a needle or that it has one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these parts all four together, then push the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a small coin;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitch suits the man, and I sewed a wound that one had in the abdomen, which was injured by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in length, and it had come out of the intestines two palms in length, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I fetched the intestine then when it had been dead for 23 hours, and the wound was sewn until the 15th day, and I treated it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I applied to the wound cotton twice a day, and washed it with warm water until he was healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper manners of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and sew the edge of the part from the outside to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the heart of one side to the other, then leave the head of the thread or the seam or where you have sewn the needle, and make it pierce the other part of the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as well as the felt-maker makes the felts, and that you leave once the seam of one side, and take it up from the other, until the suture is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of suture, which the Gauls call their own, is thus: as some do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one edge of the seam to the other edge, in a certain way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Put a needle or point of the thread close to the flesh, and make it pierce the flesh gently, and leave the two edges of the seam;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the upper part just to that inner part, between the two edges of the seam;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other of the upper part just to that inner part, into the two other edges of the thread that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst manner of fracture and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says that if this rupture is proven by testimony, one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and it is known that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the sewing is more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the artery has moved, then reset the intestine and the gut;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder made from birthwort, and if the artery has moved, then apply some ointment that is suitable, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they pull the thread, and are squeezed the veins, and the muscles;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you don't have medicine, apply on it, as much as the beginning of the gum, cotton wool, and change it twice a day until it is healthy;
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need other medicines in many treatments when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not become connected to the main members, then it is good that you soften the wool with oil of hot temperature, or with rose oil, and put it between the shoulders, and detach from the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if there is pain or inflammation in the belly, and it often happens, then they are given a cluster of black wine, and also if the inflammation reaches the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and it is known that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is injured, and it is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the closeness of its nature to the kidneys.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the serum from the wound is healthy, then it puts it back as it is, like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and turns towards yellow or black, then you must take out the part that has turned black, so that the decay of blood does not come, for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the groin, and put the two bones hanging from the part below the wound until the end to alleviate the extraction when the serum flows, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the treatment of the swelling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is wounded, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some cases, because I have seen that a man was wounded or pierced through the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right of the stomach, and became swollen and formed a fistula, and thus issued the digestion and the gas;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to apply subtle remedies until he was healthy, and the limbs were sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him whole, I doubted that the sickness was not bad in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no point of pain, but remained in better disposition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in a certain manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take the ends of the large wounds, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the wound has covered the mouth, if you put it on the two lips, so that it constricts its mouth shut;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then sew the head, and hold it so that it cannot come undone, then put another suture after in the same manner as before, until the wound is all stitched;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This head sticks in the intestine, and brings no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this thread of intestine that is very clean, and then tie to the head of this thread a subtle twisted flax thread, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and return it to its route;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of treatment of fevers is not further than according to the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and large, especially when it is in one of the intestinal grazes, there is neither art nor health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is known that every wound or abscess, when it suppurates, is universally called "fistula", and especially when it is hollow and has a cavity.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to true nodulation a hard and white tumor, where one does not feel pain, and it is as hollow as the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes its cavity is clear and empty, and other times it is thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and other times quite large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and it does not close, this is not except by one of the VIII causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has hard flesh within, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or it has too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the limb is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region has slow digestion, and delayed health, and is weakened by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or it has veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the symptoms, and the treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is suitable that I make you know the treatment of fistula which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the kidneys, or to the spleen, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous sanitation, and there is no lack of labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if it has any fistula that does not come near the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you examine it, take a probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, if you seek;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a subtle probe of fluff, because the fluff will fold around the twist;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well examine it with probes, then cleanse it through one of the openings, for the moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then examine it gently with your finger, to see if there is bone or nerve, and if it is deeply seated, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press, and the place where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the limb where it is, and if it is lacking in joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the limbs that I have told you, then cauterize according to what I have told you, and remove the faulty and corrupted flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as it is healthy, and if the fistula is well perforated straight through, then you should cauterize deeply as much as you can, then I put moist tents with sharp medicine, and push them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous flesh that remains within;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments of healthy oil and fat, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healthy with that, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or sinew does not hinder or harm the main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, then remove it as much as the decay is entire, then treat with cauterizing iron as long as it is unhealthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healthy, and the wound remains as before, know that you are not a good doctor unless you proceed to cauterize;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it is uncovered and seek as much as you are at the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the limb;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not so, know that the decay is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to let Nature take its course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with forceps, then extract it with an instrument suitable for that purpose, and if there are many bones, then pull out the third, not leaving one behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cauterize and moisturize and heat, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then put on the wound a warm poultice of decayed matter, and let it stay until the limbs are decayed around the bones, and then they will release the bones more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as the thigh or leg, then only remove the decayed matter until the blackness is all that remains of the bone, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of corrupted flesh, and it comes near to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is necessary to cut and cauterize near the corrupted area, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of about thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the humors came to the leg, and it became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no reason to bleed by opening a vein.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physicians in their foolishness opened so much that the abscesses burst open, and they ran out a lot of humors, and it became fistulous, and there came a lot of holes through which flowed both bowel and body moisture;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians treated the cure for two years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands, so that I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what was flowing through the holes from the large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pushed a probe into one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one vein came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I then hastened, and cut into one of the perforations as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption went right to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I washed what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for that which I had removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not suture;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then began again, and found the bone as before, and found that the corruption continued in the bone, and washed it, and then removed it, and prepared to suture the limb;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not put my hand inside a palm of the bone, and pulled it back with all its strength, then restored it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and quickly, and no longer needed to repeat the work because of the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For with the evacuation of blood often, but it was entirely healed, and a hard callus formed on the bone, and was of good disposition and had no discomfort or harm from all of this, neither in eating nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take the bandage, and bind at the head of the bone that is broken, and instruct him to hold it up high;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another bandage on the thigh thicker than the first one, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone, and stretch the skin, so that you draw the corrupt flesh to the bottom, and discover the flesh on the place where you see the sore, so that the sore does not touch the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a wad or a bundle under the bone to support the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary then to sit as one can see and feel the corruption, and to sit again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover the flesh entirely;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put a wad underneath, and then sit from one part to the other with the corruption, and let the sitting be as long as the corruption is, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and be the bone or it contains from the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand, or the knuckle of the foot, it is a very strong thing, but nonetheless it is necessary that you inquire into this corrosion, as it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve do not make a countercondition;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incision and the bones to be cut are many, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of the holes, and their thickness and thinness, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, it is necessary to prepare each instrument for its similar work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and be aware that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument that you need according to what is necessary for it.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may dislocate either from an internal cause or from a cauterization by fire;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have applied medicine to that corrosion through the treatment of medicines, and they are not beneficial, then it is necessary to amputate that member up to where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes either by death or by wickedness, which is greater, from the defect of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the members become black, as if they were burned by fire, and after the blackness, there comes a corruption of member to member, and it takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you are bitten by a serpent, and it is by the venom of certain beasts, such as the scorpion of the sea and viper and similar things, if the corrosion is in the head of the pain, then cauterize, and do not give respite to come near the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes near the hand, then cauterize at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come near the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then cauterize at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy or ointment that is worth the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and all this is done when the corrosion comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then cauterize after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cauterize the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, cut at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to leave the patient to death;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way to cut or saw the limb is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one of the assistants downwards, and another assistant upwards, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ligaments with a spatula as wide as possible, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw, and put on each part a dressing of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy flesh, and comes to the patient another lesion and a new abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if a flow of blood comes when you make an incision, then cauterize the flesh immediately, or put on some constricting powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is accomplished, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in his dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a blackness that seemed to be a burning of fire, and this corrosion first came into his right foot, until it took over the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to amputate the foot, and was cured;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after that the corruption returned to the right hand, and he came to me, and I applied things which rebound after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to amputate his hand, but I refused, because I had hope of counteracting the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and feared that if he cut his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the arm was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired of it, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not seen that this has been done before except for those who are in the profession.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to the flesh and remains so long that it makes a large collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it breaks and bursts, and the pus spills out, and leaves the flesh pale, like a useless vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is underneath is as thin as delicate cloth, and does not adhere to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called " eczema", and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so enlarged that it comes just to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so that you should cut around the entire wound, and likewise when it is subtle, like a delicate cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not hinder because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you think that the skin will hinder, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then heal it by applying a poultice:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the abscesses are large, and the bowel that is in it is of foul odor, then make a poultice of Egyptian medicine which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take vitriol, and oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and put the mixture in a vessel on the fire, until the medicine becomes red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take from that according to necessity, and make it into a poultice and in the middle, and inject it into the bottom, and hold the perineum;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine be in for 2 hours, then extract it while squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the chest is relieved, and the pus is thrown out;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes an injection of hot ashes is made, when this medicine is not available, and it is that you take ashes from the trunk of a vine, and throw hot water on them, then filter it, and inject it, until you know that the chest is well cleaned;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the hot ashes, then inject a mixture of hot and mild where there is a bit of powdered litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	You should clarify with honey and wine mixture, that the honeys have properties of purifying and washing, and the wines make the blood more acidic;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you have ensured that the blood is well purified, then clarify with what makes charcoal appear in it, and you take a plaster made of diafoun powder, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clarify with certain medications and oils, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of the oils;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the hole of the abscess is small, and the cane of the syringe cannot enter, then widen it with a needle a little, and put in a piece of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then sew it and leave only as much room as the syringe can enter, and if the hole that the pus comes from is above, then cut below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in the depth, do not let it protrude outward;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the belly as you wish, arrange it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest place it is, for when the bowel is deep, do not let it protrude outward and if you cannot cover the belly as you wish, arrange it in such a manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowel will run lightly downward, and do not let anything of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and apply a bandage of linen that covers the whole wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the forces of the wound with a plaster, and make a hole in it one finger wider than before, then apply ointment gently on another bandage according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound of the belly to alleviate the bowel, and do not remove the large bandage outside except after several days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is on the perforated wound of the breast, often throws up to expel the pus, and knows what comes out of the pus, if it is venom or a pouce or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in a certain manner and you see the nature that rises from the wound of the sore, then know that the wounds are healing, and approach the health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, if change the other dressing, and renew the application.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the sore throws up undigested pus after many days, know that the sore is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long tension, do not despair of the health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose tardiness in removing the blackness from their wounds, and of those that do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if his bowels are not digesting well after many days, know that the breasts are not making it better;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to make it better, and it is delayed, then apply dry medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diafoint ointment, for there is a large portion of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diafoint ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the juice of equal vintage wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then prepare the confection and put it to use;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same mixture makes a sweet cooked fat, when diafoint ointment is not available, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and pound it, and powder it on the honey while it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then in glue I spread, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes I administer an aristologist's draught, and roots of lis celestial, which is as fine as flour of vetches and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simples or of composites:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make into powder, and put on the honey that I mentioned, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is prolonged, and it is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep-seated, and makes an impression on the bone, or the hard members, or the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment for a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panaritium is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the thumb or hand, or foot, or by accident arises in other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is inflamed, and no care is taken, then the abscess comes, and it runs and discharges pus as long as it runs to the root of the fingernail, and by chance it discharges entirely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches to the bone, as long as a painful and foul-smelling ulcer appears, and the head is swollen with widespread pain, and its color turns putrid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment is of no benefit, then it is necessary that you cut off all the surplus flesh that remains from the fingernail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is of great aid if the bone is sound, and the fingernail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the fingernail presses on the flesh, and causes it to swell, and become black, then it is necessary that you put something under the fingernail to raise the flesh, and push it upwards, and cut away the dead flesh subtly and lightly, and apply to the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the joints as long as they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, chop it off, and apply force, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the decayed part, cut it off in the same way as it was said before, then heal it as long as it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is swollen, and bruised, and he feels great pain, then it is necessary that you should heal it first;
