puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the sharp and pointed thorn of the splinter, cutting across, and beware that the cut does not reach the flesh which is beneath the nail, because the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on it to calm it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the soreness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two bones that grow in the hands of certain men by accident are all cartilaginous, and by accident they have a ligament or they have bones, and sometimes they have an angle, and none of them grow from the root of the joint, where the growth is in certain nodes of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those that grow on one knuckle of the finger do not move, and those that grow at the joint of the finger, by accident, do move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the one that is cartilaginous is light, in a ligament manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Size it at its root with a wide spatulum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those that grow at the root of the joint are painful to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	it holds onto the flesh.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one that grows on the last knuckle of the finger, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh round about to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for that, then cure it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pain that comes to both sides together comes from birth, or from a sudden wound, or from a burn of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you treat the sudden pain, then you must repair it according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two moist cloths or towels soaked in oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two subtle pieces of cloth, as long as the member is swollen, if it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sudden pain comes to one of its sides with the palm, then treat that sudden pain as it is necessary.
des vils	of the ulcers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Ulcers are thick veined wounds full of melancholic superfluities that come in many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes purging of the bile, and then the blood of the basilisk.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is where they cup, and pull out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open the vein, and pull it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	raise the leg of the patient who is very cold and weak, as much as the thick blood becomes subtle, then pull the leg of the sick from the knee to the hip joint up to the part below the groin;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cup the vein in one place, or in two or in three, with a large cut, then elevate and pull out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the patient can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the physician instructs him to anoint himself with black tar and meat juice;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommends evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The elevations of it are in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the leg of the patient, if it has many hairs, then shave or wash them, and rub the leg with warm water until it becomes red, and the veins become swollen;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then apply it directly to the vein of the loin at the head of the groin, or on the part below the thigh;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the loin, and scratch the vein from each part, as much as it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and then it becomes red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems also like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then cut the razor to the bone, as long as it is raised from the skin, and then anoint it with a light ointment, then cut it on the other side with three fingers;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scratch the skin on the vein as much as it appears, then raise it with the razor, as you have done, and anoint it with another ointment, as you have done before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another incision, or several if you are skilled in the trade, then raise it, and cut to the bottom of the foot, then draw and raise it up to the second incision;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it out from incision to incision, as long as it goes freely, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot draw and raise it, then put a strong double thread on the needle, and raise and draw it, and cut underneath the bone, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as long as it will go;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and guard that she does not fall, for if she falls, one cannot treat or lift her, and it comes to harm the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it all, put on the place of the wound a moistened linen cloth in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the eyelid is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one treats the eyelid is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not injure the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curvature, for if it were subtle, it would injure the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is obstructed in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs nor trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it grows in another part than the legs, and this comes from the decay that rises from under the skin, as it does within the body of snakes and worms, obstructed between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that there comes on the leg a great inflammation, then the limbs change, and the vein starts to come out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plaster one and a half inches thick, and the knot, and leave the plaster on the leg, and all the times that it is necessary to remove it, then wrap around the plaster and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely removed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, then it grows back into the flesh, and causes abscess and rot in the limb, and a very bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of which thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it happens sometimes with this vein when it is treated with 5 or 6 fingers of length, and a vessel comes to me, from which it issues 6 fingers of length, and when you cut it, then the artery protrudes or bursts, and pierces all the way through, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and apply to the limb medications that promote putrefaction for no day, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And often at this vein there are many pains, and similarly when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which the pain decreases;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure the ills then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects the cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body rising and descending, and is felt well when it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it appears, and falls out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by purulence of certain humors, such as come worms and snakes and earthworms and intestinal worms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, one cannot be certain that when it will heal:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	it is necessary then that you tie the limb above and below with a strong string tightly, then cut above and treat the wound, and if the vein is deep in the flesh, and you do not touch it, cauterize it with fire, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm that it does, is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near to the eye, hold back from him the eyebrow forcefully, then cut above, and treat the wound;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use on the patient a treatment of purging of the body with solutive medicines for the bad and putrid humors, and beware of eating putrid and corrupting foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called in our land "vapour", and is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and a little after, I saw it move up as if a worm to the shoulder, swifter than anything, like living silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from that place, and fixes in the shoulder, and then a little after runs throughout the whole body, until it comes into the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it would turn back inside the body, as I had seen it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had seen many times that they moved well from one painful place to another, but I had not seen it in this way, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins, and for this reason the aforementioned constriction appeared;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it did not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, it appears as we have said, if the joint is lifted up and down repeatedly, and then cut into it so that the aforementioned constriction at the place of the vein is forced out;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the limb;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see with your eyes, then treat what troubles the intestines, such as foul-smelling pills, and pills of serpent, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the limbs of the body where they are found.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some which have large heads, and small ones, and barbed, and jagged;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two edges, and of those that have handles, and of those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and the one that falls in no member falls according to two methods:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in principal members it falls, such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then on any of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it happens that you warn them of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when there is a bad sign that does not appear to me, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the thread that is on the brain, is when there is a split and a rupture and a turning away and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and perverting of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and by chance it is without force to the nostrils, or to the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it affects the speech and the voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes a white discharge resembling pus, and also a foul-smelling flux like that of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this is a sign that appears, if you hold back from the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls or passes, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it was stuck in a hard thing, not at all empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves like the pus, and cuts out black blood, and brings on coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	the wounds then are without doubt a sign that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that strikes the arm is that without great pain, a discharge comes out from the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the patient changes color, and breathes deeply and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the covering of the foot, it is painful for the little toes;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great suffering and pain and shortness of breath;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound some undigested thing of the flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the belly, and it perforates the intestine with a hole through the gut, there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels a strong pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	it is known that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the joint and the spine of the back and the forearm and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happens to me, for that which you must do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happens to the man that an arrowhead remains in the arm at the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out, and pulled it from another part below the fat of the ear, and it was healthy without any mess.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And pulled from one wound an arrow that the fat of the eye had underneath the skin underneath, and the arrow was embedded, and could not be felt except the point towards the trunk, and it was a large arrow of a Turkish bow, with the iron rod without barbs;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The play was over, and no evil accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with barbs:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I will shave the beard, and I will make it subtle as I do the trick, and the Christians will be healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled an arrow from the man, which had entered his belly, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and since thirty days had passed, his condition had not changed;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out strongly, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw the man to whom an arrow had fallen into his back, and the wound was swollen above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and his natural functions were not changed, nor did I find any damage in any of his natural organs.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, into whom an arrow had fallen into his face, and the wound was swollen;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and therefore remains thus suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And he pulled an arrow from the hand of the prince, the king, which had been shot in behind his knee, and was somewhat leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to the cure after it had been shot for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it with a subtle touch, and could not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a piercing and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow, I put on the place an emplaster made with attractives and digestives, because the limbs did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the limb appeared to me to be that of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on the wound, and treated the injured limb, and it remained there for a long time, until the arrowhead was felt inside his body;
et il le me dist.	and it pressed against his bladder.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound caustic corrosive medicine for a long time, until it was covered, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which had adhered to the flesh;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted in the opening of the wound with that caustic medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it exceeded the limits within four months, and then I cleared the wound so that I joined the tendons, and the muscles on one side and the other, but could not exit;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to refine and engineer devices, until I took the arrow with the tendons well made, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, so that I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you should base your treatment on what I say, for books cannot grasp everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters understand well only a little of what is said, and on what is present and deficient, they find new work, and new instruments, in the discernment of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not issue from the limbs or are fixed unless it is according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which shoots forth where it enters, is an arrow entering into fleshy parts, and shoots forth from them sometimes.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not heal now, then let it be until the flesh is putrid around it, and the pus is alleviated.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot come out, then let it be for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will heal, and if it does not heal, then pierce around it with a subtle instrument, until the tissue around it is enlarged, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrowhead is fixed in the bone of the head, and comes near to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned above to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	then do not treat it immediately, but let it be until it is even after some days, for if the arrowhead comes near to the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not deeply embedded in the bone, and does not come close to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad accidents, then the engine of traction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply embedded in this and cannot be pulled out, then administer traction around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the limb of the body so that one cannot see it, then search for it everywhere;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrowhead, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then push it in so that the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow that it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck between the two parts of the bow that you hold, and then break or crush the ears of the arrow, until you can pull it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, that you pull it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until the surrounding flesh is purified, then pull it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you contradict, then remember what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision of the nerve and of the vein, and advise how you can pull the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient in the same position as when the arrow fell, for this is the greatest aid that it should be, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears with something of it, or the skin is swollen in the place if one sees or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then upwards, as long as the tongs can grasp, and then extract:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if blood flows now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand around, as long as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction as long as it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the fist of the arrow is in, thrust it to all the fist;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the bone is fractured, and you wish to administer a poultice, if you administer the instrument gently, then the tip of the arrowhead enters into the flesh of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then apply force, and if the arrow is deeply embedded, then you push the instrument to the point of entry, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it requires.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow penetrates the foot or the thigh or the belly or the bladder or the ribcage, and it is protruding, and you can cut around it, then you cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if it is necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs with which one treats the arrowheads are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many methods:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed tool is like the feather of a bird, to prick at the point of the arrow, as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pricking and for extracting is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which one bleeds are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two vessels which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the little vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two sinews which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augenherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one usually bleeds are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the head, and lay people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and lay people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is on the right side, and the laymen call it "vein of the belly", and it is near the ribcage, and it is the one from which they bleed, which visibly appears on the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the thumb and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and on the foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curvature of the left hip, and the second is the saphena which is on the right side of the shin;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nesse", which is on the shin of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps against ancient coughs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the blood, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a coarse cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then press the patient's neck to a vice, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in the two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	take the bandages from your back, and where you feel the pulse beneath your back, it is a sign of an abscess;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancette and push it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand at all the vein above, and cut and the skin and the vein well, two fingers from the traverse, and make the blood come out as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then constrict and bind, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is useful for migraines, and swelling, and customary ophthalmia, and on the body of the watery eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the blood is such as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patients strain their neck, so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and they feel the pulse at the bottom of the back, and then they indicate by bending;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then he raises the heart on the vein above at the back of the index finger, and puts the lancet below, and raises the vein above, and cuts it, just as you have done with the other veins, and makes the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then he releases the patient, and puts his back on the vein for an hour, then applies a cotton pad;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then let the abscess form, and leave it until it is healthy;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their treatment and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bloodletting of the head for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the disease constricts the neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "incisor", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and strike with the back of your hand, or with another thing, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then untie from the patient the neck, and leave the vein until it is healthy and sometimes open one of the large veins.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	In no way does it matter that the flames are too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the vein is pierced through, because the bone is near, and by chance the flame breaks when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The veins of the two arms that are in the two shoulders help with the eyes, and the forehead, and the redness, and the hearing in the ear, and the ailments of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their vein is that the patients stretch their neck while turning some ligament, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the vein, and let the vein be pierced through, a little bit long from the flame a little wide, because it does not have a point to burn.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make an incision of blood, as much as you are able in your profession, and then bind on the wound, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The blood of the vein that is born from the ankle is good for pain, and for hidden sores, and for face diseases, such as emigraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the blood is such that the patient should pull their neck, then pull their ankle with their left hand, and take the subtle flame long, and insert it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well by itself, and the blood will start to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it bleed too deeply, and make the blood flow according to its need, then leave it for a night, because it is very hot when restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two elbows helps with the narrowing of the thigh, and with the beginning of paralysis, and with many diseases, and with petechia, and with corrosions, and with herpes, and with eczema;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the sore is such that the patient stretches his neck to one side and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the masters be at the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then let the vein of the elbow be cut somewhat broadly, then let the blood flow moderately, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then perform the same on the other vein, then untie the ligature, and hold the middle veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, so that the wound is clean.
de la sainie des leivres	of the sore of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sores of the veins of the lips above are identified by a collar in the mouth, and a corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and pain of teeth and inside.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	cut then one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and also make it the same for the veins that are above and below, because it is a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the blood below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the blood of the head, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the blood is such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks down at each corner to see a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Feel then one and the other, and do not press too deeply in, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm that one feels commonly are felt in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by pricking to the whole flamed meridian, or subtly olive-like as when the veins are being cut, and it is called "aneuil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flamed meridian is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it has the task of opening the superficial veins with a large amount of visible blood, and which contain a lot of blood and muddiness;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the form of the flame of olive oil
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is for purging the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purging of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are in the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the purger to purge wisely, and that he beware of the artery that is above.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one should not press the flame, but cut with a cauterizing iron.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica vein does not appear manifestly, then it is necessary that you dissect it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Or you want some vein of his, or you will find in his arm the vein with blood.
elle apert manifestement;	It appears manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the blow to the weak ankle, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know the location of the vein, then it is necessary that you stretch the arm, so that you touch the spot as soon as you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then bend the joint of the elbow, and then lift the arm, and strike the vein of the weak ankle;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the swollen spot, for it is near the artery:
eschui la donques.	beware of the gift.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding high up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if it is without strain, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Raise the arm, and let it be, and do not move the patient's;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be on a poultice, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if it is without strain, and it does not help, and the medicine is not prescribed for you, then cut the artery that is open, because the head of the treatment;
et estainche li sans.	and strains the joint.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a splint of fistula, and bind it, and take one of the parts and place it well next to the other joint;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the joint is strained, it's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that constrict blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stitches are not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the positioning of the string of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The blood of the vein in the middle helps since it draws blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon that he be warned by the nerve which is beneath, and if he cuts too deeply, and he touches the nerve, and it becomes inflamed and the wound becomes grievous, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in any man because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you know the sinews of the instrument;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve with your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, thus the wound is very long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting of the head helps, which draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed at the olive vein or at the martian vein, for it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest vein, and not to harm anything if one fails the first time, and then try again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance one will find a good vein for some men, when one fails the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to one's thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is not done except to preserve health and to avoid impending illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are on the elbow:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	these are to know, the cephalic, the middle, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, and in autumn, and in April after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three times a day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered for illnesses has no determined hour, but rather when need is of day or night, at all hours and in every tension;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to bleed children up to thirteen years, nor a woman carrying fruit for more than four months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should the old who have passed sixty years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some want to purge themselves, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that they empty the intestines of a light cluster, if it has many retained filths, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful dung from the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor does it purify one who is too full of meats, nor one who is drunk, as long as he is full of it, nor the dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and let one beware of purging after a colic passion, and vomiting, and deterioration of the stomach, and multiplying of the womb in women, and from travail, from vigil, and from fasting, and that which is all virtue, or through a thing of the arm or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then refine the humors, if they are not coarse, through meats and through beverages and through medicines, so that you have them in a subtle power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly let the blood flow, and this blood is from the vein that runs between the thigh and the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself during the day from effort, and from excess, and from dislocation, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be joyful and happy, and let the vein that is being bled be higher than the one being bled from, and rub the arm two or three times, then gently pull the vein upwards, for when it is too narrow or too wide, it cannot be treated;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the body with the hands, until the veins swell, and feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then anoint the veins with a little warm oil, then put his right hand on the left vein below the body a little where he wishes to bleed, so that the vein does not flee and fail to be pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that are as tight as cords in the sausage, and if it is of those that are full of wind, so that when one puts on the flame, it draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, the wound is too tight, because of which it is necessary that the sausages be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then one begins again a little below that place or above the handle, if the places are not weakened.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the places are weakened, and the patient is spitting, let him a day or two, and do not lift the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	for it will bring on an abscess of the armpit.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter into a bath, then recommend the sauna if it pleases them;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the perforation is small, or the wound cuts subtly and you doubt that it does not issue as much blood as you see, then make that same perforation to the entire flame directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and a little haste in the work, so that the limbs are not weakened;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this happens often, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb weakened, do not recommend the sauna, and put a little oil on it, for it alleviates the body of blood, and is bad in this limb the oil that the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and administer the oil in each sauna where you bathe the veins, to staunch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing makes for a triangle and a bump of eyes, when one puts it on the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If the blood is subtle and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not healthy outside except for the times when the opening of the vein is small, then hasten, and put on the wound a wet sponge in water and in vinegar a little warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the wound after some hours any blackness or greenness, do not touch it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you want, put on a dressing of garlic or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there occurs an abscess and swelling at the wound of the basilic vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put your hand on it, and if you find the flesh soft to the pressure of the hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Beware then that you do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance in short time without the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make the plaster dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each one blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it be until it becomes subtle;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is weak and lacking, and needs extraction of blood, that a larger wound be made for him, and that the wounds be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this kind of injury is saved from decay of blood and from damage of the nerve, and is better than the injury of the lung or of the side.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body lacks at the injury site, it is good to give soft poultice made with juice of crushed pomegranates;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is hot, apply three or four times a treatment of blood; And if it is of cold complexion, apply before the injury a soft poultice made with syrup of honeyed musk, or in syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicories, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it throbs at the injury site, after the issue of a lot of blood, it is good that he drink broth of beef, and subtle scented syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to purge his arm, and to bleed another time, then it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of its virtue continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to purge his arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong body, then he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to bleed from another part, then he should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	then it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and to widen the aperture as far as it reaches to the lungs;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	After you have regarded all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come into the lung, and this happens many times, when the bleeder is neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see the arm become dislocated, to make blood come out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly upon;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, that he should extend the arm hastily, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him alone until it bleeds a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you touch the point of the flame, until the blood that has congealed at the opening of the vein comes out, and put some warm oil on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood a second time, then let it be from the same limb, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is called by the name of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in warm water, as long as the vessels are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then the blood is let from the middle, neither from the width nor from the length;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the punctures be wide, and let the blood be drawn well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot flow out, then put the hand in warm water, and let the blood run into the water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salve of the right hand is worth all the medicines for the ills of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and soak it in warm water, until the vein becomes swollen, so that one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you cut it across, and you cut it from top to bottom, it does not harm anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not cut too deeply in the flesh, for the nerves are already half stripped of their covering, and then put the hand in warm water, if the wound is congealed, and cannot be drained.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let out as much blood as is necessary, then apply oil to the vein and bind it tightly at once, and make a plaster of each of these.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve on the left hand is good for illness of the spleen, and do everything just as I have told you regarding the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The vein of the spleen is useful for all the diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the liver, and retention of fluids, and disease of the kidneys, and of the thighs and of the old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its vein is that it draws out the disease from the foot into cold water, and rubs on the vein until it pierces, and binds above the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot in come many kidneys;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then bleed where the larger kidney is, or at the ankle, which is most useful.
