Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed on the foot, you will be cured of the kidneys that are below, and the vein of traversing as in cupping;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the blood flow out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then reset the stone in the urine, and let the vein be well emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first application of the plasters fails, then recommend the second one a little afterwards, for the limbs are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the spleen of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limbs of the sciatic vein are at the fork of the thigh, and its application is worth the pain of the hip, when it is because of hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its application is that the patient should be in a bath, and squeeze four fingers above the fork while twisting, because otherwise the vein does not appear;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, then apply the plaster in all the ways that you can, and penetrating through;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the joint is healthy, and it is much put back into place by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not turn it, then press any vein that opens at the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard against the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make the blood flow as much as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	the knee is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wounds of the stomach
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Wounds are made from horns, or from iron, or from a stick;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and wound is treated in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cauterizing and attracting blood, or without cauterizing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this wound treatment without cauterization is in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Where it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and venesection which is done by striking and by extraction of blood if it is done in the 13 parts of the body, of which one is all in sum the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the vein at the bottom of the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the veins of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the veins on the ankles;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the veins in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the veins of the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the veins of the two calves;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the venesection does not treat any point of blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason one does not become weak, as one does when the blood of a vein is let;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable that it be administered, nor to any fire nor sensation of fire, in any illness which comes from excess, as long as the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is necessary to administer an enema, or due to habit, we will give it to them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and at every tension;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have need to be administered an enema, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience excess and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who spit a mouthful of blood, and have a swollen tongue, and vomit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see in their sleep blood and pain and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is amidst the month, we command to ventilate after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saliva of the nose helps with the bitterness of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary except after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in the place of the saliva of the cephalic, and it is not necessary except for those who are of a cold complexion in habit, or who have diarrhea, because that causes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for the old people to use it, nor for those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often blow their nose, become oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to put the ventilator a little more below due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation in the neck is at the place of the vein and of the jugular and basilic vein, and for this reason it is good for the straining of the foot, and for the fissure of the channel of the forearm, and for the cough, and for the replenishment;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is good to cure a bit of swelling, because if it holds too tightly, it injures the bladder or stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilations of the two ribs of the neck are good for the pains of the head, and for ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for the pain of the roots of the teeth, and it is at the place of the vein of the basilic;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is good that you instruct the surgeon to press his hand on the spot, so he does not cut the artery, and does not make the blood vessels overflow with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The bad smells from the mouth are equivalent to a disease of the mouth, and to a rotting of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the healing of the sores of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bad smells of the entrails are equivalent to a disease that comes from heat and from fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The bad smells of the body are equivalent to as much as three veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon that he should not make too deep an incision, because the leg is nude of flesh, and knows badly nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The bad smell that is on the backside is equivalent to hemorrhoids of the foundation, and to similar diseases, and it is necessary that the bad smell be large, and be of blood, so that it has need of being well treated;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it was subtle, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The ulcers of the legs heal openly, for they attract blood from the whole body, and are worth the old pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and bring back the flesh;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in place of two sponges, and of two trunks, and altogether they weaken the body after long use, and bring about a foul discharge in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the ulcer treatment is that you apply it first gently, and press moderately, and put it hastily, and rub equally, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and the appearance of blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then do it firmly, and put back the ulcers, and take heed to the condition of the body, for there are some who have such hot blood, and pure pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to refine the passage of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to strike the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to let a little blood and a little, then we suffice with only one time.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we repeat often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then strike deeply, and stop there where it seems that the vein has been pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who has narrow pores, that you apply to the limbs ointments which are aperitive and dissolutive:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	It is a remedy made from violet oil, or from almond oil, or from the oil of cucumber seeds.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and it is also in ivy, made from oil of cress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is coarse and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and has large pores, it does not require any oil, but rather to be washed after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for one who has a lot of moisture, rosewater is lifted, or myrtle water, and sumach, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities rise with old wine, or with water of sewing, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or with other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not suitable to apply a poultice of fennel before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the poulticing, and it is suitable that he should be warmed, when he must be poulticed and when he is poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who have a bilious nature, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is suitable that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce with vinegar, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little nuts, and flesh of chestnuts, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and a little ginger, and a little cinnamon and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the more it is ventilated, one should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men three or four nutsmeg before or after ventilation, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be refined, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cuppings that are applied without piercing are those that are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and to the abdomen, and to the belly and the navel and the loins and the hip, because these members do not suffer from being pierced, and it is not done for fear of attracting blood from member to member, as we place on the breasts when there is an excess of blood;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To treat the viscosity that is in the limb, as we apply warm poultices to the stomach and to the navel to soften the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and to treat the pain, when there is obstruction or stone, so treat by its attractive virtue by adventure the obstruction, or remove the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one applies it to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these poultices are administered empty to suck up as much moisture;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fever, and sometimes plain or with hot water, as in illnesses of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the poultice with hot and humid water, or with water in which one has cooked suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered to the fever is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and it has on the outer side of the middle a small perforation, as if to put a needle through, and let it be of silk thread, soft in front so that it does not bother the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it has in the middle a crosswise rod of silk or iron, to hold a bandage in place, and they are large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who wear them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the ulcers of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must then put this ulcer on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the bandage of wax or the plaster, and put it in the ulcer across the rod that is in the ulcer, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the ulcer so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and let your fingers be on the orifice that we have spoken of, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes in, and remove the ventouse;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the plaster as before, and recommend it often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse therefore which is administered for disease of the pleura, to all that has no verge or orifice, and is not administered except when it is full of water, and is put on the member as soon as;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without them being administered except on members where one cannot put ventouses due to their smallness, such as the lips and cheeks, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare flesh wounds, such as fingers or nails, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is such that when you find sweet smooth things in narrow passages, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a narrow sweet nut, as long as they are familiar, and have nothing in the stomach;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed of vein and of intestine, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the things;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flattened, and will gush out, if it is the liver or one can put intestine, if one puts it, for it is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the liver of the axle, and then of the narrow passage, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the liver is too thin afterwards near the body of the things, then wrap it in a linen cloth in a cold narrow passage, and put on, until the thing is strengthened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is multiple, then put on a mixture of vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it is dried;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put on the limb warm poultices of peeled beans, and let them be there until they adhere to the limb, then it will dry now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you are a master of more skill, then take other bloodlettings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the bloodlettings do not want to take, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or you stick in a needle until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling, then powder on a bit of powdered aloe and ground celery, or cinder, and they will dry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and of dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish people despise this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they learned any letter;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is foreign in our land, for I have never found any good;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except for the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the treatments that are needed, as I have done in these two previous chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the discourse and the chapters where the wise man sets his understanding, and stays on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or shaking comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to anoint the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents you from doing so, such as weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the tension is not very warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid cold and raw foods, that is to say cold joints, and flesh of goat and of deer, and do not drink wine, and avoid eating fatty and greasy foods, and do not fill oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you are not in doubt of a hot abscess, or of an accumulation of matter in the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his previous bad governance, he will relapse.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to mend, it is necessary that the patient be fed with foods that promote thick nourishment, where he has viscosity, such as roasted pork and bacon, and fried and boiled meats, and liver and entrails of beasts, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For poor nourishment shows meager and worse the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit cannot well mend or reunite according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but for a cure, reset the broken bone and the large tendons that are separated and join the member together, so it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and he not the whole use of his work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish him with coarse foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that come from a blow, and another from a fall, such as the cut of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture is all just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own engine, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory recalls in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by what the joints are twisted, and appears well by swelling, and sounds hollow to the touch of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no crookedness in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no point of fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but he can well have a crookedness, or a fissure, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move the limb, but apply medicines that come next, and then gently extract it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which comes in a joint, and are the two parts disjoined, it is necessary to put them now in an equal place, so that abscesses do not come;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, then let be no movement, until the abscess is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it even to the bone that you can lift gently and wisely, and know that the restoration of the bone is easier than the restorations of the skull or where there are fragments;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold tight, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone breaks into pieces, stop the flow of two parts, whether it is the hand or foot, or to your hand if it is small members, or to the cords, or to one cord and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are disjointed, reset by all means the additions in their places at the joint that you can, and take care that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two parts of the bones according to their proper forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if the dressing is done properly, and it is not strained too much, nor pressed as those who make them come by their work causing abscess and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, instruct the patient well that they should not move it, neither while awake nor while asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limb is so secured that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it is necessary to put it in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is placed straight, so that crookedness does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of a broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to envelop them with soft and subtle bandages;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those which are thick, like the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	if it is necessary to envelop with a large and hard linen bandage, because the wide bandages press the whole limb, and constrain equally on all sides, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind it tightly with light bandages, three or four according to the member, and constrain the hand a little on the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and constrain less, than the fracture, then loosen a little the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little and often, as much as you press on the healthy part of the limb, then take another bandage, and turn around again above the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and constrain moderately, neither too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first bandage above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the lips of the wound a swab of linen or cloths, as long as it is all even, then tie all with bandages above, and then put your instruments well made on, if there isn't an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is a swelling or an abscess, then put on it something that appeases the abscess with heat, and which reduces the swelling, and leaves some days passing;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then strip your instruments, and let them be of the humidity of a large cane wisely, or of wood from which one makes the cleavers, or of branches of palm, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the instrument which one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is necessary for the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold steady on the stables as you did in the first treatise, then tie a thread underneath, as in the first treatise on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the more constricted it is underneath, the less there is;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and be of flax or linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish men who make their ligatures with twisted flax cords, and it is a great error, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that it has between each staple less than two fingers of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is troubled by the edges of the stables after the constriction on their healthy limbs, then put underneath them a dressing of flax or linen cloth, so that it does not chafe.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the chest is broken, I will tell you about the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not matter to stretch these broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it does not matter to put these splints for five days or seven, or more according to the severity of the abscess and the healing that follows.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the method of ancient splints for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and knead it with a little water, and put this paste, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of plaster for restoring fractures in many dispositions, and also for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster for restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the sprain:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take barberry and ladanum and enula and asafoetida and Arabic gum and mastic, a dram of each;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, a half dram of each;
alechil VIIII З.;	of electuary eight drams;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make into powder, and mix with the white of egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the temperament of the man is cold, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores the broken bones, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mastic and viscammum, a dram of each;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, eight drams of each;
acaice VI З.;	of acacia six drams;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil Armenian terrapin, and crush well, and mix with water or broth of beef.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat joints and bones dislocated from their places, and alleviate the overriding pain, and the fracture of the bone, and the bruising.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen cloth, and the marrow in oil and cooked, and put on the body.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore the limb, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses, and properly easing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to treat fractures that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves, and earthworm leaves, and crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat the fracture of the bone and to alleviate the pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of violets, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of peas, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and pound, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are swollen, mix it with water of moist coriander or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of violets, and seeds of flax, balustre, melilot, and sanzuc, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and pound, and mix with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken limb anything to restore it except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be between two things not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems reasonable to apply to the broken limb, for restoration, warm and slightly hot things, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of applying a plaster that is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and roots of hemlock, or feathers of birds, and viminal and equal quantities, and crush them, and make a plaster with the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then dissolve it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone of their body damaged;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it does not dissolve by itself in a short time.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the body, or swelling, without rest or relief, then hasten, and dissolve it, and remove the plaster immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	Take a light cloth, and a sea sponge moistened, and dip it in water, and lift the limb up, until the itching stops, and the pain is alleviated;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply to it a dry, moistened with water or rose oil, linen cloth, and tie it on with a nut, until you are sure of a warm abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain be eased, then apply a subtle plaster, and a little poultice, and do not bind it as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and apply subtly until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the warm abscess and redness and pain and swelling are all gone, and you have applied a poultice and a bandage, then reapply it, just as you did previously.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the limb any of what we have said, do not force the dislocation further after three or four or five or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture becomes solid and the adjustment of the flesh closes in;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than at first, and bind its vein, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that it cannot be restored;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	raise then the cold water bath, every time you dislocate it, and let it be so for three days, and loosen a little the ligature;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work then cut the dead flesh from the limb, and straighten what the foolish surgeons do, who twist the member awry;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is harmful, and such operations are to be feared, and I do not see anything other than giving pain and operating wrongly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various kinds of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures exist, and there are various shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures made by the blow of a sword, and the collarbone breaks the bone near the shoulder which is separated from the bone, as if done with an axe or club;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "ax-blow" or "hewing".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword cuts through the bone from the underside, and it is called this kind of fracture "cut-off" or "severance".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound from these two fractures is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has a sunken-in strike, or crack or blow to the head, or fall onto stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing wound, which approaches just to the web that is beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this is a wound whether large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has grown into the bone as subtle as a straw, and the split is small, and for this reason it is called this breakage "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or a similar thing, and it makes the piece of bone go in, and the bones are split as the blacksmiths do when they strike on the anvils;
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the stones within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this especially happens to those who have moist heads or bones, such as a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these ways of breakage that small pieces are separated as these;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the extraction from them, and the inquiry with tongs, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like similarity is known by that which when one discovers the bone, and rubs against it, if the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, beware of accidents from the disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and tension, and palpitations, and sharp fever, and the eyes becoming disordered and red, and other similar things in various conditions, then one cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightful accident, and you hope for health, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to expose the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, likewise that the torn part of the bone is corrupted, and come the accidents that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you suture the fractured part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you hold the head of the injured patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if a discharge of blood comes to uncover the bone, or a abscess breaks, use what aid is necessary, and it is that you fill the hole with moistened cloths in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the broken abscess is appeased, and be assured of the discharge of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then the treatment begins with the bone to the vein, and it is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is that you cut at the narrow incision in front, and it is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then you make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in working lightly, so you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, it is necessary that you pierce through it, in such a way that you make incisions with cauterization tools, not too deep so they do not penetrate beyond the bone of the head, and should have near the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have many, so that each one comes into their place of the spine, so that you have supporters for all tests;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three manners of supporters:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one supporter on the bone, and turn to your two hands as long as you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the supporter on another part a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with incisions the space of the bone which is between the parts, and do this more subtly than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the spleen.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and drawn, it is necessary that you make the instrument that remains of the bone to all other similar instruments like an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more delicate and more subtle than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or any shells, then lightly touch the bones to one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tenderness and caution that we have spoken of.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another manner of work is what the Gauls call, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it holds very strongly, and this is its property.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where it is broken or separated, so that when you have discovered that part, then put on the head of this lancet-shaped instrument, whose form is this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the affected part is in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer from above, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it adheres to the bone, gently lift it, for one lifts it well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut just above, and it has small pieces, then it is necessary to render that asperity, and to remove the scales with a subtle rasp which you must have in various quantities, to apply on each part the most convenient, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with large rasps, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease from doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other haircuts and subtle breakages, it is necessary that you make adjustments according to their growth.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and it's something that isn't easily answered by one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is deep, then you should take a piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another doubled piece of linen in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first piece of linen;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can, so that you don't hurt the wound, then apply another linen on top, and don't strain it more than necessary to touch the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be this way for a day or two, until the aposteme's heat is alleviated, then undo it, and apply medicines such as roots of lily, and powder of vetches, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer at the same time medicines without causing numbness;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and beware that the wound is immediately clean, so you do not let in the inflammation, nor let it suppurate, for when pus assembles on the cloth of the brain, it corrupts and decays, and brings to the patient great evil;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts on the sore a caustic thing, it becomes worse by above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, that no evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if black discharge does not come forth by the medicine that one has applied, which virtue it has, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one thread, and put it on the sore;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then for the cure of manners of cures it is suitable, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	It is known that sometimes the two parts of the knee are broken, where one part alone is broken, because there are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that joint is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it becomes swollen or twisted, and then becomes diseased.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is suitable that you apply your little bandage or plaster of the knee, and put equal to that break inside your bandage, and in the pouch by default, until the knee regains its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the knee, and the joint cannot come to its place, it is suitable that you put it even at the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another one similar, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscessed ulcers are appeased, then bandage the head of the knee with tendons of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bandage the other part, where the fracture is;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the tendons be so thick that they fill the holes of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And direct someone to moisten the tendons in butter, and move each joint.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but rather that they should be moistened with a concoction of egg and powder of mallow.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then let the tendon alone, until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes the swelling pushes out the eyes from their orbits, and if the bandage is too tight inside, and it holds the fracture, and the patient breathes with difficulty;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or make a hole so that you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the eyes while you are operating, then put cotton moistened with rose oil, or in a pouch of theriac.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster made from flour of cypress, and powder of incense, mixed with water of roses, then put on light poultices, and do not tie around the eyes;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the eyes is small, and it breaks into tiny pieces, then extract the suitable fragments from that, then sew the crack, and the treatment of things that cause black discharge, and swelling, like plasters and ointments suitable for that;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has no thickness of new flesh, then apply the treatment of tents, and put on clean dressings, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken apart, and there is no open wound, and the breakage is only slight, and it is not broken into two pieces, but rather fractured within, then one can feel it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breakage is on the right side, that you put your right index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the breakage is on the left jaw, then put your right index finger, and gently push the breakage from inside, and hold the other jaw with the other hand from outside, and set it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jaw is separated into two parts, then it is necessary that you administer extension to the two parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth are shaken or broken, or loose, hold them in place with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the bruised jaw a kerchief, and put on a double bandage.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the bandage a large steel plate well made, or a piece of leather equally long and wide as the jaw, and tie it to the head that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the fracture is changing, then untie it on the third day, and then reset to its place what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster on it, made from powder of mill with abundant egg white or flour of sage, after you have applied the kerchief;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on the plaster a light linen cloth, and if the plasters stick, and the condition of the patient does not change, let it be until it is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if it has a fracture and wound together, restore the bare piece of bone in being bone;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of the fracture shows dubious congealings to that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with a flame according to necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have bone all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound, if it is large, and put on it suitable plasters to that, to bind flesh, until it be healed.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture breaks several times beforehand, towards the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	When it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are fragments, and it is more difficult to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is such that when the break is without wound, you should have two attendants, so that one holds the injured area where the break has occurred;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the break equal with your two hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch further, then put between the shoulder and the patient a round ball of cloth, or of wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the injured area, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you put the break in place as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out of the ditch, because it comes from deep, then it is necessary that the patient put his hand on his hip, and put the medium of the shoulder in the hollow of the ear, and turn the lower part of the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then take the fracture in your hands, and if you pull it straight, it is necessary that you split it apart;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any means, then cut it with one of the incisions that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you put within the shoulder this instrument, to guard the spleen:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it seems a spoon, and is not too heavy, and should be as wide as it is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the instrument;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, just like the routing of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the routing is small, or you doubt the abscess is hot, then fill the wound with dressings and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten the dressing in rose oil and in vinegar and in wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without a wound and without a cut, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powdered millstone and of buffalo's urine, and apply light bandages, and put a woolen sponge under the bottom, if you have the skill;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage of a palm's width, then put a double cloth on the stupes, and apply the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin stick of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the end of the bandage is hanging;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and undo the healthy shoulder, and undo the diseased shoulder;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture firmly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on the fractured bone, then check every day, and when the ligaments relax, then restrain it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient sit on his back, and put when he sleeps a small pillow under the shoulder, to lift the joint upwards;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the fracture of the clavicle is alleviated by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and no bad accident comes from it, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then reapply the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and hold it in place and let it be, until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is most often restored within twenty-eight days, and in less than eight weeks.
