de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the shoulder fractures or dislocates and does not stay in place, and is not held except by touching;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the bandage conforms to the shape of the fracture, and you reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the limb powder made from millstone with a little wool, and light compresses, and put on a double bandage;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a broad and subtle stick, a little broader than the shoulder, and if the stick is dislocated it moves in no place of the shoulder, unless one applies that stick with bandages of linen, so that the stick is steady.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it with a large bandage firmly, so that the stick does not move from its place, and look at the limb each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it becomes dislocated, restrain it, and put the stick back in its place, and let the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is accomplished, then disbandage it, and be careful, for it is not good to keep the splint on too lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and forms a point under the heart, then make an incision, and cut the bone, and do what we have said in the case of breaking through the apoplectic abscess with heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The feet are sometimes broken in the middle, but that happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often at the toe.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to the bottom, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and weakness, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the bowel in the broken bone, and loosens the senses completely.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient often places on their back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the edges of the two ribs with his hands, and subtly adjusts to put everything in its proper place, as much as you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and dressings above the subtle splint of salt, or other light paste, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the linen round to the back, and hold it tight, and check every hour the liver, and if it breaks, then hold it fast;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to dissolve, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and dissolve it, and scrape off the plaster, and address that which has come from various methods of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the plaster, and hold it fast as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	It is known that the fracture of the ribs does not come except from heavy blows to the back, and to the inner chest, and they do not break except because they are brittle;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the bone feels well to the examination by the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you make equal the fracture, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and extract a splinter, if you have it in your profession.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of the ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as from a pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and reaches to the tips of the fingers, and all and vomits great clots of blood, and it is a grievous sickness, and the old men have put great skill.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is one of those who say that it is necessary to administer winds that swell the belly, to push out the fracture from the spleen.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, that hot abscesses do not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it be soothed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one puts poultices on the body, to suck out the humor, and it seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	In every way, it is doubtful whether the veins attract the excesses to the body due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of them say that one must cover the body with a warm woolen cloth soaked in hot oil, and apply bandages between the ribs to evenly distribute the remedy around, then it will be cured by the treatment of pleurisy, of diet and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear by the bone that touches the membrane, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the body of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put a instrument in place to guard the lung;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and gently pull it back, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a posthernia abscess comes, then put on moistened cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the affected area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat meanwhile the area of what is necessary for the abscess, and let the healing scabs form on the affected side where it should, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and it happens that it breaks;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take heed if you see their hands made soft and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if the nerves die and feel well when one presses on them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the disease will be cured, if one applies a remedy.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take care to see if the feet are soft, and if the injury is in the hands, and on the back there is swelling and unwanted evacuation.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has it above his stomach, then there is unwanted evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is swollen above his back and he wants to sit, then he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	then do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this injury does not come to the veins, then it is a thing of lesser concern.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you should apply if it has a hot abscess, put on the spine oil of rose or oil of muesef of herb, as long as it is applied gently;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone dislocates, then it is necessary to apply to the heart;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and reset the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat with application of gum, until he is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "head of the elbow", then bend your pouchet with your left hand, and place it even with the other hand on your arm, then put the plaster and the steel on it, if you have the skill;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then pull it tight, and if there is a dislocated bone, put it back in place, and reset it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It happens that the bone of the thigh is fractured, and if it happens, then it does not happen with a small amount of swelling at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it causes pain for a long time, and declines to the worst, and comes to the patient with pain at the leg, and piercing, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you put your hand on it, as long as you are above the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and feel what the breakage and the shape of it are;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the breakage is at the head only, then put equal to that breakage, as long as it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is for a long time, or it declines inward, then make the patient lie on their belly, as long as the restoration of that breakage appears.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, put on a plaster, then put on a stick of wood or bone, and hold the fracture steady, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the plaster to the body below the ribs, until the bandage is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient that he should sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a hot abscess comes, do not touch it, until the hot abscess has cooled, and put on what we have previously mentioned;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and constrain it as is necessary, if there is no other bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The joints are that which is between the joint and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	except for one thing, which is to take a smooth club according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends of the bandages, and throw them over high, and let the patient sit on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then put his arm broken on the club, until it comes to the joint, and have in the middle a curvature of the club, then throw over some heavy thing where the ministers extend downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the physician's hands together equal to the fracture, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his shoulder, and ties the hand to his neck, then instructs the ministers that one touches what is on the fracture with their hands, and the others touch below everything to the bandage, and each extends to its own part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forced, then hold the bandage below the fracture, and on the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you put one bandage below the joint, and the other towards the hollow, below the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the hollow, then it is necessary to put a bandage lightly, without pressure, until the fracture is even on the limb, and on the hollow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then put even the fracture, as it is necessary, and hold it, for if abscesses come, they will not develop.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses do come, then do not hold it tight for seven days, and put on a soft cloth and oil of rose, until the abscess is softened;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	After the extraction, and the manner of the extraction is such that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm with the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage, and bind it to the shoulder, and to the arm, so that the arm is in its natural position, unless something would displace it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone will not move, then use splints, and put on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers' width, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers from each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then bind to the splints, thus as I have said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, stronger and less constricting.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the numbness of the limbs, and the constriction, as we have said, in the work that you restore the broken member, and you suspect the hot abscess, leave it to heal until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then examine each for three days the ligament, which if it is not inflamed or swollen does not come to the limb, or the nourishments cannot come to the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it adheres, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, do not force the dislocation further that after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the shoulder a cushion made of wool equally, and examine each hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken member does not move, nor are the ligaments softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If it is received through the virtue of medicine, and the food is given that we have previously placed before them, in such a manner that the food should be at the first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it starts to take again, it should be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be taken back in 40 days from all;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must dislocate and administer baths and medicines of joints for the body to receive.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the fracture is bad and swollen, it will take 40 days or 2 months to dislocate.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of 2 bones, which are called the two "fleshly" ones, one of which is small, and it is the one that joins the shoulder;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is out of joint, towards the little back;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance break the large fragile ligament, or the small one, and by chance it heals together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small fragile ligaments are broken, the restoration is gentle, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are broken and healed together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's the small fragile ligament that is broken alone, then it is necessary to stretch gently, and to put in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's the large ligament, then it is necessary to stretch more strongly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch on the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and let the small fingers be lower than the other fingers, and let the patient cross their arms over themselves, and the cushion in front of them higher, so that the patient suffers no strain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the minister's arm to the part dislocated from his hand, or to the elbow, and another minister to the other at the upper arm.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the limb in its proper place, according to its natural form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is a fragment that the heart does not want to release, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint and a bandage, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if the breakage involves a wound, I have spoken of it in a special chapter;
si pren la cure.	take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration appear abscesses or ulcers, apply a plaster made from oil rosat and white wax, which should be neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and you touch the plaster gently from above, until the abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the dressing, and apply a plaster made from powder of millstone with enough wax, then put on the stents, and let the stent of the fracture be stronger, and a little larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it should have six stents or arms in several positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	let the fracture be in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold more firmly on the fracture than other parts, and all the less when touching, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the dressings that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor harsh;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, which it is strained by, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And look after the limb and the tendon after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wrap the limb with warm cloth, until that itching is alleviated;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be tightly wrapped to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the constriction, and if the tendons are softened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, apply a remedy.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And beware that the nourishments cannot reach the limb, because it is too constricted, then you should loosen it a little, and let it be for some days, until the nourishment spreads, and then constrict it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not untie it for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or when entering, then he puts his hands on his neck, and his neck is even, and beware of movement and of degeneration, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the composition and complexion of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have said, there are few fractures, and it does not come but rather a sprain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the joint of the hand is fractured or sprained, then it is necessary that the patient sits crossed, and sits upright before him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then put his hand on the extended toe, and extend the fractured bones, and put them even with the mirrors, as long as they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply a plaster and poultices, if an abscess does not come, then he puts a stake according to the quantity of the humor;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is in the middle of the belly of the sole, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to his fractured foot;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bind with a long cloth, and let the stake be of wood sufficiently thick as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the finger, it is necessary that you put a stake on top, and another below in the sole of the foot, so that the hand is straight and upright, then tie all around the hand, and tighten the cloth between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to one of the two bones, it is the shoulders, set them even, as it is necessary;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and strain with the sole of the foot, and if you see that a small right splint is put in place to raise the fracture, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in the other bones, such as in the index finger or one of the others, set it even, and bind it with the healthy bone that is next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all together, as seems best, or you put on a splint, just like a shoulder;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the treatment of hot abscesses, and dry those that come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns to the front and back;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is thus on one side of the fracture, and another beside it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient puts his hands on his face, then each assistant extends his hand to his part equally;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it is when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, let one of the assistants be at the knee, and the other assistants beside the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the assistant be at the knee, and let the extension be below;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the doctor's hands on the bone equally with his two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if there are abscesses or wounds.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it be soothed, then return to your work and to its treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The ligature is made in a similar way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove the superfluous, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the ankle, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the thread come out above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put on the fracture these, and put a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make even the pressure, then begin to tie firmly two or three turns around the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the more you go up from the fracture, the less it is constricted;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then understand about the two heads of the thread that you have placed between the thigh and the hip, and in the third the stitches that are underneath, then return to the bottom at the head of the thread, until you come up against the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it tight, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, then let there not come abscess or swelling or any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then untie it, and treat what has come, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if it has pieces of bone that are piercing, then reset them in their place, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then reset by cutting the limb, and pulling forcibly;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the hip is broken thus where one puts stitches, as in the shoulder and or arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	In all ways, during restoration thus made not to harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in a day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the complications.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the wrinkle of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the wrinkle of the knee there is little breaking, but it often cracks.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's nothing but a fissure, or a perforation, and there is a complete wound, and without a wound, and this is felt very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when one puts back in place that which is broken to its joints, as long as it is assembled with what one can;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and you put on a round steel, if you are skilled in the art, and hold it as needed, then observe all the treatments that we have said for other fractures, such as abscesses, heat, and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Put to each accident what is suitable for it, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Be aware that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right "tibia", and the other is called "fibula";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it has the same kind of fracture as the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is all alike. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns entirely.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and the goiter is visible;
et torne desoz.	and turns to one side.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension, and put it in place, and lay the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but however, it is necessary for the fracture to be set, and there are many pieces, so that the extension may be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the wing according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two splints of split wood that enclose the thigh on one side and the other, and are as long as the thigh from the knee to the buttocks;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap it in two cloths, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle, and to this binding do not let the thigh lean to the right or left, and thus it is well;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and let no one administer a bandage as long as the thigh, and it is of wood, and put it on the thigh to prevent movement, and properly make this in the fracture or where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or some other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you treat him as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bone of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle comes no fracture, but to the bone of the foot comes sometimes a fracture and to the two bones, and it does not matter that they are shattered in many dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture of the bone of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, just as if he were standing, and then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, then press down until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the plaster and bandages above, and put on the bottom of the foot near the two tendons a small tablet, then bind the foot firmly, then that you have wrapped the dressings around, and other things that you have need of.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the ligament, for you will find the bones even, whether broken, whether dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are some of the fingers broken, restore them, as we have said regarding the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a little wider, then put beneath the foot that table that I have spoken of, and hold it firmly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each finger a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and hold the table beneath the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be fixed on top of the table beyond the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, since we have spoken of them.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone in the hip of the woman is broken, if it is made to swell, then it is inclined to the back part, and held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the bath with warm water of the disease of the ulcer, and in it put a large stone as I said;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then undress the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then push the ulcer, until it comes to the entrance of the womb, and the bone returns with the stone;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the ulcer, and when she has urinated, put it back on her, and do this for seven days or within;
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If it will be restored the fracture, and you see, take a bladder of goat, and tie to the hole a chain, and put all the bladder in the nostril.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the chain strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the nostril will restore the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and let it be thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the hip is fractured, either of the man or of the woman, it should be restored thus as we have said for the bone of the thigh;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who puts their study and effort, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the rod, when it is broken, take a handful of ivy and tie up the rod;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it in rags around, and let it be three days or therein, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of a fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the healings that we have spoken of bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then anoint with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then recommence to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, if apostems of the ulcer does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if apostems of the ulcer does come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the apostems are appeased, and do not touch it on the third day nor on the fourth, for you would cause bad accidents to come.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the heart of the uncovered side, then you must put it in place lightly with your hands, to small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not suitable for putting in place with your hands, then reset it with this instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 fingers in length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the surgeon to take three or four, according to what is needed for each treatment of a fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let them be rough and a little thick, so they do not float in the compression on the member of your work, and let them be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary that the curved tongs are put on the head of the apparent bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and beat it once, as long as it is straight, and even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the muscles cannot grasp the bone well, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, so that the muscles have possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an instrument suitable for that, whether to incise or sew, according to your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what remains in the bone of splinters and small shards.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do this until it is in its place, then wrap it in a bandage soaked in black styptic wine, and properly if it is in a splint.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound, such as a cerote or other things that have oil, so that it does not bring about purulence and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer these things after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted with the dressing;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have foolish doctors done this, and brought about death or corruption to the patient, or made them ill at least;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the dressing be softer and more gentle than other dressings.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that an evil accident will occur, as we have said, and you feel pain in the body, then it is not necessary to put these things on;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, on the body of the wound, durable cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days an ulcer at the wound, remove what you had applied on it, and put on a healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment Tetrapharmacum and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you anoint the member two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is swollen and sore.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members be wrapped in such a way that the ulcer can be covered lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but instead discharges pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, because of which it is necessary that you examine the wound with a probe, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or another kind of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is written in its chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not touch it, for many times death comes, but let it be until it forms a callus.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	By chance it will close itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound, if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the wounds that come onto the abscess
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times they come after the sanctification of the fracture, especially when it's near the joint, and the worst thing is to see the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance it cannot make the limbs perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then that the wounds are fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer medicines that draw in, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and other similar things, then take one of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that draws in, or with vinegar of rose, or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the nut with tourniquets, and hold it well, and do not untie it for a long time;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then untie it, and begin another, until the knot is loosened;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you hold on a well-made piece of plaster;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the properties of plaster are such that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot has already converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above it, and make the excess appear;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you render it to some ease, until it be loosened, and the treatment until it be healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of a limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains after the limbs are weak and delicate, then it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	of the fact that one is because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because it had too many ties, and the nourishments could not come to the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or from a multitude of roughness;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or from too great movements, not in their proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you should make the patient eat, and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in it;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, and give joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then apply poultice to the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and roughness of bitter tar, until the nourishment runs to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb becomes twisted after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limbs are twisted after the resetting, and the broken bones are exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if you do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these practices are to be blamed, and great evils come from them, and death often results;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the swellings and the pain are fresh, then it is necessary that they be treated with warm water, or that softening herbs be applied, such as leaves of violets, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening plaster, such as a well-made diaquilon, and take the muscle of violet, and mix it with the fat of a goose or oil of cypress, and apply the plaster;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or you take fat figs, and crush them with juice of coltsfoot, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with a moist hand.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And restore movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortured area is inflamed and hardened, like stone, and needs to be opened with iron, then you should carefully cut just to the bone, subtly and lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put caution and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here is treated the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if necessary now bring back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one is late, the limbs become swollen, and by chance, if one resets them to their proper place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is not suitable for one to move it to the place where it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times it brings on spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	in any case, when this happens, make the patient healthy, then let him be, until the abscesses or tumors are appeased;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the member from the cold and oil, then reset it lightly, and treat each member as its cure will come into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated and twisted, and the dislocation of both is in two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	Where they are a little swollen at their joints, and slightly softened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Where they are entirely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be held, nor can the mouth be closed, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns more quickly with multiple remedies.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and complicated, then you must reset it promptly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the minister guides the head of the patient, and puts his fingers in the pocket of one of their hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on the lower jaw;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and let the other two hands be separated, to put them in alignment;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient that they should loosen their jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mire (physician) put it (the joint) back even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reset is grievous, similarly if these are the two jaws together, then they should be raised with warm water and oil, until they are reset lightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Nor do we speak of resetting, as we have already said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well without softening, then put on dressings moistened with a mixture made of oil rosat and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head be held between two cushions, so that they do not move either to the right or left, nor exert themselves to chew, but take light food, until the pains are eased, and the jaws are numb;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then chew what he wants lightly, and does not exert himself to open the mouth to eat and to drink, until the jaw is well cleaned and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their place in one hour, and are not converted to their uses, then there comes fever and habitual sweating, and by chance diarrhea, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of impending death;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he whom it happens to, dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fracture
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fracture cannot dislocate from the costal cartilage within the continuity of the rib and the breast, and is sometimes dislocated at the defect, and it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient puts his shoulder against his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the limb firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and bind it tight, and constrain it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the part which is turned towards the hip cannot become dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not, and if it becomes dislocated at any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the plaster and bind it tight, and constrain it, and instruct the patient to rest as long as he is healthy;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and likewise the head of the spine is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is when it becomes dislocated at the part above the armpit;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the foot;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates at the upper part, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind at the shoulder, and does not dislocate within at the kidneys;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocates downward toward the armpit, especially to those who have little flesh, for to them the joint jumps with sudden movement;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	to those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance some men have a blow or fracture, and the shoulder is swollen with a hot abscess, and it is thought that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary then that you examine it, until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it is downward toward the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a visible diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the bone touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were one bone;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his shoulders, nor move with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is new, or if the patient is healthy.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the ministers raise the patient's hand upwards, then put their fingers below the bone, and lift the joint forcibly upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister raises the hand and stretches it upwards, then puts it back in place;
si venra hastanment.	if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in two days afterwards, then it is necessary for the patient to be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and let the anointing be soothing and softening, such as a decoction of leaves and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be anointed;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then let the patient be rubbed on their back, and put under the shoulder a cushion of wool even, not too soft nor too hard, then put the mirror to his heel on the cushion, and lift the head of the patient's shoulder gently, and pull out the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another servant should hold the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder returns now, and you see if it is reset according to this method:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you have someone present who is stronger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And let it be straight towards the costal area, and push the shoulder downwards from the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upwards, so that the patient's weight hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And let another assistant pull the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too lightweight, then hang with him something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reset it in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is as if one fixes the long bone in the ground, so that the head is reset like the pistol, and is not too large nor too slender;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then let it be put under the patient, but so that he has draped clothing above, and the patient is standing from the length of the trunk;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then let his hand be extended downwards from the other side, formed, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then make this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take the size of 4 fingers in width and 3 fingers in length, which has the head rounded to enter inside at the bottom of the joint, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then put on the head of the fist a soft cloth, so that the fist does not hurt the patient, then put it under the joint of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and stretch your arm to the fist of the length, and put the shoulder on the fist, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on one of the sides of a wide chair, and let the other hand hang below, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint now returns to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that may be, then you must put under the joint an even layer of flax, then put on the plaster mixed with powder of mill, and incense and oil of  rose, on all the shoulder and around, then strain under the joint a little vinegar, and turn the linen on the plaster, and press the hand to its neck, and let the other hand remain in place.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he massages a little, so that the limb is comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then massage more after 5 or 7 days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is hardened and does not become softened, then it will not heal.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has accumulated, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations to three parts, as it is written before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is of the chest, and the shoulders, or the back, is made by push, and extension of hands, and one administers another ointment;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cures it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.
