And after the healing, stiffness comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, so the patient must bathe it many times, until that stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	It is known that the joint of the elbow is dislocated at the points, and at the points it returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated on all sides, and likewise in front and behind, and the dislocation is not put back, for one sees it well and feels it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the injured limb with the sound one, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is strained, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it so that the abscesses of the wound are removed, for if the abscesses were to come, it would be grievous to reset;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reset completely, especially when it is in the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can reset it, that you extend its hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and its arms are expanded, and the hands of the thigh according to the injured limb, above and below, and bind the joint to its skin together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it happens when one doubles their hand to their hand, and makes from the root of the palm the joint that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers stretch the arm, and two ministers hold it, so that it does not move during the stretching;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped it in a double cloth that is long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the mire joins the joint to their hand, then anoint with some oil to soften the joint, then bind the joint firmly, until it returns to health;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, then put on a dry plaster with wool and a bandage, and bind firmly, and hang the arm from the neck of the patient, and leave it for some hours, then undo it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is closed in its place, then untie the bandage, and let it go;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not bind well, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and let it be for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if it feels gritty after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is soothed;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put on the joint a poultice of greasy wool, then let it stay for a day and a night, then remove it, and make it enter into a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the poultice back on, and then enter into a bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times, until it is healthy;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, then put on a warm poultice made with butter, and strain it;
si revenra a sa disposition.	if it returns to its natural position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the displacement is slight, more than the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place quickly, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the limbs are not swollen, or that an abscess does not develop.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reduction is done by placing the injured hand on a table, and extending the fingers of the hand, and the thumb placed evenly, so that it places its palm on the surface of the joint, and bends until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is necessary for you to check if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient's hand on a table at extension and flexion.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then put the patient's back of his hand on the table, and let the doctor put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then strain the poultices that soothe abscesses and let be without re-inflammation.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after some hours, then the joint remains twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not harm the patient more than necessary, as long as the hand is swollen, and cannot strain anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other remedy but to constrain by cauterization of the case, and by chance it is not worth anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then constrain it and let it be five hours, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some swelling, then warm the wrist with warm water, and rub it until it is sound.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated to each side, sometimes to the back of the palm or to the front;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then extend the fingers, and push the dislocation to your pouched hands as far as it will go, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjoined;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and let it be for two days, and then put it even with the hair;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and anoint the body, as we have said, and untie the hair, and make it move, and anoint the body again;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is straight, and also do the same if it is dislocated in the stomach of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healthy;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do the same, when it is dislocated in another area.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade from the back or neck is dislocated, where there are often multiple dislocations, if there is no point of treatment, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the evacuations come out by itself without will, and cannot be held, and often some members are softened, or the two hips or the two arms.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the urine changes to four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	That which changes at the bottom is called "glucosuria" or "diabetes":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment is that you should reward yourself that the glucosuria has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no point of cure or healing for all of it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from a fall or from blows or similar things, the ancient manners of cures said with grand words, where there is no great profit in all of it;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed treatments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the glucosuria that comes to the penis in front, there is neither engineering nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly to the two sides, and one cannot cure that which comes from the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient must be stretched on their face in a straight line, and have their spine restrained from them, so they do not bend;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then fix the one thigh to the ground firmly, and the other to the feet, and tie a bandage around the shoulders of the patient, and one to the hips, and to the knees, and to the calves;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two attendants hold the bandages, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two thighs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be held firmly, the thigh as we have said, and the doctor puts his palms on the spine firmly, until it slips back into place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not slip back into place with this treatment, take a table three feet long, and shave the surface, and let the patient be on their side, and put the end of the table under the shoulder, then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the mirror to his feet on the other head of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, make it for the turner who turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you fix two splints at the head of the patient's arm with a great bandage, and towards the feet the other two, and between each splint, separated and apart, a palm of space of a hand's length;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each splint one hole, where the turner runs, and be the splint firmly on the ground, so that it does not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between the two splints have one turning splint, on which the turns run, and have in the two turners two small splints of a hand's length, for turning the turner;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the string that is between the splints to the turner towards the head, and the other string towards the feet to the other turner, and each of the attendants turns his turner with all the string, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on a plaster made with a lot of vinegar, and then the poultices, and then the handle of a tablet of three inches in length, which should press on the place of the dislocation and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use subtle nursing on the patient, until they are healthy;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if anything comes at the end of the treatment, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the handle that we mentioned earlier;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes it is necessary to administer a piece of flax, and sometimes the appearance comes in the upper part of the spine at the back, and beware that it may be a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that breaks, for which one should not have high hopes:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	By accident, death comes.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocation of the thigh
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	It is known that the joints of the thigh and the joints of the shoulder do not come out except for dislocations only, nor does it happen to them as it does to other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the thigh is dislocated in four ways:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	downward and upward, forward and backward;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and most dislocations are downward, and few are dislocated forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the sign of this dislocation downward is that when one joins the sick thigh with the sound one, it is longer, and the patient's knee opens more than the sound one, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the ground;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the member that is affected by a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh-bone comes out of place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who has come to the defect, is that this accident is contrary to what is before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who has come to the fore, are that his leg is well according to the accomplishment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	In any case, do not double the knee joint with pain, and if one wants to make it move, then it cannot beforehand, and it retains its urine, and inflames the groin, and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has come behind, are that he cannot stretch his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is out of place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The recall of this kind of dislocation is that you recognize if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, then there is no cure for it;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it does not matter that he has a presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four manners of dislocation, you should hasten to turn the joint, and stretch within and without, and move to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	by chance if it returns, and there is no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong minister, and strongly stretch the leg with two hands, or with a bandage that is tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister stretches his hand from below in such a way that he pushes his hands under his armpits, then tightens with a soft bandage above the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another pulls the head of the leg;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If that is not so, then it is necessary to apply a treatment to its similarity.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder joint, then you must support the patient on his healthy side, then put the linen on the root of the thigh, and the limb which is above the hip, then stretch the linen upwards towards the hip, and towards the strength;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then take another cloth under his arms, and encircle the large limb of the diseased thigh, and stretch it to the opposite firm;
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot constrain it in the manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the diseased person together with a strong linen bandage under the two heels, and under the two knees, and let the diseased leg be stretched two fingers more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then let it hang from the head of a post, and let it be two arms length above the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then instruct the minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister be hanging with the patient, who will strongly hold the thigh, because the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is downward, thus the patient's thigh, as we have said concerning one who has a gibbosity, and pull the limb upward from the patient's own leg, and also from the hip;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two clamps, one at the head and the other at the feet, then fix one clamp between the thighs of the patient in the middle;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and let wet cloths be placed inside, so that they do not hurt the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the surgeon puts his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on a table, and press thus as we have said in the gibbosity, and give the patient a bandage on the injured side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the sick thigh immediately, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and put his hand on the healthy side against the sick ankle, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is backwards, it is not necessary to stretch the sick part downwards, nor lift it up from the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip was dislocated backwards, as we have said concerning the lying down on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it be on its face, and the limb stretched out as we have said before, and one must press on the joint against the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be at a point when the patient's legs are even, and they will be equal;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the hips, and apply a plaster, and bind with a bandage, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let it rest for three or four days, then undo it, and apply the plaster on top;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, bind them as before, and let them be for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then undo it, and make him walk gently, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward, outward, and backward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and does not dislocate at all forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if it does not adhere to his hip, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your two, then bend the two sides of the knee to form;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another servant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and you signal that he should well have his leg on his thigh lightly;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the splint on, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then undo it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not bother the patient to get up, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until he is healed;
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of it are that the ankle is weak, and swollen in front of the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the reduction of it is easy, and the hand one extends gently with their hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from the whole, then you must have the patient sit straight, and pull inwards firmly by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the foot with your right hand, and then with the left hand twice, then pull it upwards, and nicely push the foot upwards;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, it's good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then resume the work, because it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return thus, make the patient sit on the ground with his back straight, and pin the passage firmly to the ground between his thighs, and tie the drapels around, so that the patient does not escape;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then hold the thigh of the minister, and another minister stretches the foot to his hands or to the lien, so that he ties it on the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then stretch each minister equally, and let the passages be between the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when they stretch it;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then put the mire equally to the dislocation with his hands, and another minister holds the healthy thigh below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it has reached the limit, put the plaster on and apply pressure, and bind firmly, and tie the foot to the thigh, and watch the nerves that are behind the knee, so that the ligaments are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then let it be for two or three days, and if the ligaments become inflamed, then bind firmly;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then undo it on the third day or the fourth, and have the patient rest for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes beyond that limit, it is not a certainty that he will dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then it is necessary to treat them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, then it is necessary to gently stretch them without effort, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the vertebrae of the back or the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a straight table, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns to its place;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and nothing opens, then put under the sole of the foot a table at two hands, then strain firmly, and leave it three hours, then untie it;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make him rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and of dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and if you are not piteous and merciful and slow, nor harsh;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply heat at the beginning of things that induce abscesses, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscesses which are hot may subside;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, then administer things that induce abscesses with heat, and treat the wound, as it requires, with dried dressings;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is dislocation with fracture, and small bones are out of joint, then reset the bones, and do what we have said regarding simple ailments;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for it is worth more to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.
